Skewed X inactivation in a female MZ twin results in <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> . 
One of female MZ twins presented with <mark>muscular dystrophy</mark> . 
Physical examination , creatine phosphokinase levels , and muscle biopsy were consistent with <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) . 
However , because of her sex she was diagnosed as having <mark>limb - girdle muscular dystrophy</mark> . 
With cDNA probes to the <mark>DMD</mark> gene , a gene deletion was detected in the twins and their mother . 
The de novo mutation which arose in the mother was shown by novel junction fragments generated by HindIII , PstI , or TaqI when probed with cDNA8 . 
Additional evidence of a large gene deletion was given by novel SfiI junction fragments detected by probes p20 , J - Bir , and J - 66 on pulsed - field gel electrophoresis ( PFGE ) . 
Immunoblot analysis of muscle from the affected twin showed dystrophin of normal size but of reduced amount . 
Immunofluorescent visualization of dystrophin revealed foci of dystrophin - positive fibers adjacent to foci of dystrophin - negative fibers . 
These data indicate that the affected twin is a manifesting carrier of an abnormal <mark>DMD</mark> gene , her <mark>myopathy</mark> being a direct result of underexpression of dystrophin . 
Cytogenetic analysis revealed normal karyotypes , eliminating the possibility of a translocation affecting <mark>DMD</mark> gene function . 
Both linkage analysis and DNA fingerprint analysis revealed that each twin has two different X chromosomes , eliminating the possibility of <mark>uniparental disomy</mark> as a mechanism for <mark>DMD</mark> expression . 
On the basis of methylation differences of the paternal and maternal X chromosomes in these MZ twins , we propose uneven lyonization ( X chromosome inactivation ) as the underlying mechanism for disease expression in the affected female . . 
<mark>Adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> and <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> associated with partial <mark>adrenal insufficiency</mark> in three generations of a kindred . 
Four cases of <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) and one case of <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> ( <mark>AMN</mark> ) have developed in a kindred over three generations demonstrating that <mark>AMN</mark> is a clinical variant of <mark>ALD</mark> . 
Pituitary - adrenal function studies were performed in 10 family members , including two affected males and four females identified as carriers of <mark>ALD</mark> / <mark>AMN</mark> . 
No <mark>pituitary - adrenal abnormality</mark> was found in the carriers . 
However , basal morning plasma adrenocorticotropic hormone ( ACTH ) levels were markedly elevated in the two males with <mark>ALD</mark> and <mark>AMN</mark> , despite the fact that they had no clinical signs of <mark>adrenal insufficiency</mark> and that morning plasma cortisol levels and their response to maximal exogenous ACTH stimulation appeared to be normal . 
In addition , the integrated 24 - hour response to the administration were also subnormal in these two cases . 
Thus , people with <mark>ALD</mark> and <mark>AMN</mark> may have subclinical partial <mark>adrenocrotical insufficiency</mark> . 
No other <mark>endocrinologic dysfunction</mark> was identified . . 
Regional localisation of the <mark>Friedreich ataxia</mark> locus to human chromosome 9q13 - - - - q21 . 1 . 
We have previously assigned the <mark>Friedreich ataxia</mark> locus ( FRDA ) to chromosome 9 ; the current maximal lod score between FRDA and MCT112 ( D9S15 ) is greater than 50 at a recombination fraction of theta = 0 . 
The physical assignment of the locus defined by MCT112 , and hence FRDA , has not been determined , although linkage analysis of MCT112 with other chromosome 9 markers inferred a location close to the centromere . 
We have used in situ hybridisation with MCT112 , a corresponding cosmid MJ1 , and DR47 ( D9S5 ) , coupled with mapping studies on hybrid cell panels , to define more precisely the location of the disease locus . 
The in situ location of all three probes is 9q13 - - - - q21 . 
1 , distal to the variable heterochromatin region . 
Physical assignment of FRDA will allow us to identify hybrid cell lines containing the mutated gene . 
Increased high - density lipoprotein levels caused by a common cholesteryl - ester transfer protein gene mutation . 
BACKGROUND AND METHODS . 
The plasma cholesteryl - ester transfer protein ( CETP ) catalyzes the transfer of cholesteryl esters from high - density lipoprotein ( HDL ) to other lipoproteins . 
We recently described a Japanese family with increased HDL levels and <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> due to a splicing defect of the CETP gene . 
To assess the frequency and phenotype of this condition , we screened 11 additional families with high HDL levels by means of a radioimmunoassay for CETP and DNA analysis . 
RESULTS . 
We found the same CETP gene mutation in four families from three different regions of Japan . 
Analysis of restriction - fragment - length polymorphisms of the mutant CETP allele showed that all probands were homozygous for the identical haplotype . 
Family members homozygous for <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> ( n = 10 ) had moderate <mark>hypercholesterolemia</mark> ( mean total cholesterol level [ + / - SD ] , 7 . 01 + / - 0 . 83 mmol per liter ) , markedly increased levels of HDL cholesterol ( 4 . 24 + / - 1 . 01 mmol per liter ) and apolipoprotein A - I , and decreased levels of low - density lipoprotein cholesterol ( 1 . 99 + / - 0 . 80 mmol per liter ) and apolipoprotein B . 
Members heterozygous for the deficiency ( n = 20 ) , whose CETP levels were in the lower part of the normal range , had moderately increased levels of HDL cholesterol and apolipoprotein A - I and an increased ratio of HDL subclass 2 to HDL subclass 3 , as compared with unaffected family members ( 1 . 5 + / - 0 . 8 vs . 0 . 7 + / - 0 . 4 ) . 
<mark>CETP deficiency</mark> was not found in six unrelated subjects with elevated HDL cholesterol levels who were from different parts of the United States . 
CONCLUSIONS . 
<mark>CETP deficiency</mark> appears to be a frequent cause of increased HDL levels in the population of Japan , possibly because of a founder effect . 
The results that we observed in heterozygotes suggest that CETP normally plays a part in the regulation of levels of HDL subclass 2 . 
There was no evidence of <mark>premature atherosclerosis</mark> in the families with <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> . 
In fact , the lipoprotein profile of persons with <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> is potentially antiatherogenic and may be associated with an increased life span . 
Further mapping of an <mark>ataxia - telangiectasia</mark> locus to the chromosome 11q23 region . 
We recently mapped the gene for <mark>ataxia - telangiectasia</mark> group A ( ATA ) to chromosome 11q22 - 23 by linkage analysis , using the genetic markers THY1 and pYNB3 . 
12 ( D11S144 ) . 
The most likely order was cent - AT - S144 - THY1 . 
The present paper describes further mapping of the <mark>AT</mark> locus by means of a panel of 10 markers that span approximately 60 cM in the 11q22 - 23 region centered around S144 and THY1 . 
Location scores indicate that three contiguous subsegments within the [ S144 - THY1 ] segment , as well as three contiguous segments telomeric to THY1 , are each unlikely to contain the <mark>AT</mark> locus , while the more centromeric [ STMY - S144 ] segment is most likely to contain the <mark>AT</mark> locus . 
These data , together with recent refinements in the linkage and physical maps of 11q22 - 23 , place the <mark>AT</mark> locus at 11q23 . 
Recurrent <mark>meningitis</mark> in a patient with <mark>congenital deficiency of the C9 component of complement</mark> . 
First case of <mark>C9 deficiency</mark> in Europe . 
We describe the first cases , to our knowledge , of <mark>C9 deficiency</mark> in Europe that were detected in a Swiss family , of which two members - - one with a complete deficiency and the other with approximately half - normal C9 levels - - experienced <mark>bacterial meningitis</mark> . 
The index patient , a 56 - year - old white man with a history of <mark>purulent meningitis</mark> at the age of 23 years , presented with an <mark>acute meningococcal meningitis</mark> . 
No <mark>impairment of cellular immunity</mark> or <mark>immunoglobulin deficiency</mark> could be found . 
Complement assays showed a <mark>complete deficiency of the C9 component</mark> , while the other individual component levels were normal and the hemolytic activity ( measured using the CH50 assay ) was only slightly reduced . 
A family study revealed <mark>complete C9 deficiency</mark> in the patients healthy brother and half - normal C9 concentrations in his sister , his son ( who also had experienced an episode of <mark>bacterial meningitis</mark> ) , and his niece , consistent with an inherited <mark>C9 deficiency</mark> . 
This first case of <mark>recurrent meningitis</mark> in a white patient with <mark>complete C9 deficiency</mark> suggests that this <mark>complement defect</mark> may also be a risk factor for <mark>bacterial , especially neisserial , infections</mark> . . 
Detection of 98 % of <mark>DMD</mark> / <mark>BMD</mark> gene deletions by polymerase chain reaction . 
We describe oligonucleotide primer sequences that can be used to amplify eight exons plus the muscle promoter of the dystrophin gene in a single multiplex polymerase chain reaction ( PCR ) . 
When used in conjunction with an existing primer set , these two multiplex reactions detect about 98 % of deletions in patients with <mark>Duchenne or Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> , <mark>BMD</mark> ) . 
Furthermore , these primers amplify most of the exons in the deletion prone " hot spot " region around exons 44 to 53 , allowing determination of deletion endpoints and prediction of mutational effects on the translational reading frame . 
Thus , use of these PCR - based assays will allow deletion detection and prenatal diagnosis for most <mark>DMD</mark> / <mark>BMD</mark> patients in a fraction of the time required for Southern blot analysis . . 
Genetic heterogeneity at the glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase locus in southern Italy : a study on a population from the Matera district . 
Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) has been analyzed by gel electrophoresis and by quantitative assay in an unselected sample of 1524 schoolboys from the province of Matera ( Lucania ) in southern Italy . 
We have identified 43 subjects with a G6PD variant . 
Of these , 31 had severe <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> , nine had mild to moderate deficiency , and three had a non - deficient electrophoretic variant . 
The overall rate of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> was 2 . 
6 % . 
The frequency of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> , ranging from 7 . 
2 % on the Ionian Coast to zero on the eastern side of the Lucanian Apennines , appears to be inversely related to the distance of each town examined from the Ionian Coast , suggesting that this geographic distribution may reflect , at least in part , gene flow from Greek settlers . 
Biochemical characterization has shown that most of the <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> in this population is accounted for by G6PD Mediterranean . 
In addition , we have found several examples of two other known polymorphic variants ( G6PD Cagliari and G6PD A - ) ; three new polymorphic variants , G6PD Metaponto ( class III ) , G6PD Montalbano ( class III ) , and G6PD Pisticci ( class IV ) ; and two sporadic variants , G6PD Tursi ( class III ) and G6PD Ferrandina ( class II ) . 
These data provide further evidence for the marked genetic heterogeneity of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> within a relatively narrow geographic area and they prove the presence in the Italian peninsula of a gene ( GdA - ) regarded as characteristically African . 
<mark>Deficiency of the murine fifth complement component ( C5 )</mark> . 
A 2 - base pair gene deletion in a 5 ' - exon . 
To ascertain the molecular mechanism that causes murine <mark>C5 deficiency</mark> , genomic and cDNA libraries were constructed from mouse liver DNA and mRNA employing the congenic strains B10 . 
D2 / nSnJ and B10 . 
D2 / oSnJ that are sufficient and <mark>deficient for C5</mark> , respectively . 
Genomic fragments were isolated which correspond to PvuII and HindIII restriction fragment length polymorphisms associated with <mark>C5 deficiency</mark> . 
Sequence analyses demonstrated that each of these polymorphisms resulted from single base pair substitutions and that neither substitution would probably cause or contribute to the <mark>C5 deficiency</mark> . 
Sequence analyses of C5 sufficient and deficient cDNAs revealed a 2 base - pair deletion in the deficient cDNAs . 
The " TA " deletion was located near the 5 end of the cDNA . 
This deletion shifts the reading frame of the C5 mRNA so that the termination codon UGA is present 4 base pairs downstream from the deletion . 
Genomic DNA was amplified and sequenced corresponding to the area surrounding the 2 - base pair deletion . 
Six <mark>C5 - deficient</mark> strains , A / HeJ , AKR / J , DBA / 2J , NZB / B1NJ , SWR / J , and B10 . 
D2 / oSnJ , and four C5 - sufficient strains , Balb / CJ , C57Bl / 6J , DBA / 1J , and B10 . 
D2 / nSnJ , were analyzed . 
The sequencing data revealed that the 2 base pairs were deleted from the C5 gene of each deficient mouse tested but not from the C5 gene of any sufficient mouse . 
These data demonstrate that 1 ) there is an identical 2 - base pair deletion in an exon of the C5 gene in several different <mark>C5 - deficient</mark> mouse strains ; 2 ) the mRNA transcribed from the C5D gene retains this deletion ; and 3 ) this mutation should result in <mark>C5 protein deficiency</mark> . 
Molecular genetics of <mark>PKU</mark> in eastern Europe : a nonsense mutation associated with haplotype 4 of the phenylalanine hydroxylase gene . 
<mark>Phenylketonuria</mark> ( <mark>PKU</mark> ) is a <mark>genetic disorder</mark> secondary to a <mark>deficiency of hepatic phenylalanine hydroxylase</mark> ( PAH ) . 
Several mutations in the PAH gene have recently been reported , and linkage disequilibrium was observed between RFLP haplotypes and specific mutations . 
A new <mark>molecular lesion</mark> has been identified in exon 7 of the PAH gene in a Hungarian <mark>PKU</mark> patient by direct sequencing of PCR - amplified DNA . 
The C - to - T transition causes the substitution of Arg243 to a termination codon , and the mutant allele is associated with haplotype 4 of the PAH gene . 
The mutation is present in two of nine mutant haplotype 4 alleles among Eastern Europeans and is not present among Western Europeans and Asians . 
The rarity of this mutant allele and its restricted geographic distribution suggest that the mutational event occurred recently on a normal haplotype 4 background in Eastern Europe . . 
The red - green visual pigment gene region in <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> . 
Although recent data established that a specific very - long - chain fatty acyl - CoA synthetase is defective in <mark>X - linked adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) , the <mark>ALD</mark> gene is still unidentified . 
The <mark>ALD</mark> locus has been mapped to Xq28 , like the red and green color pigment genes . 
<mark>Abnormal color vision</mark> has been observed in 12 of 27 patients with <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> ( <mark>AMN</mark> ) , a milder form of <mark>ALD</mark> . 
Furthermore , rearrangements of the color vision gene cluster were found in four of eight <mark>ALD</mark> kindreds . 
This led us to propose that a single DNA rearrangement could underlie both <mark>ALD</mark> and <mark>abnormal color vision</mark> in these patients . 
Study of 34 French <mark>ALD</mark> patients failed to reveal a higher than expected frequency of green / red visual pigment rearrangements 3 to the red / green color vision gene complex . 
The previous report of such rearrangements was based on small numbers and lack of knowledge that the frequency of " abnormal " color vision arrays on molecular analysis was twice as high as expected on the basis of the frequency of <mark>phenotypic color vision defects</mark> . 
The red / green color pigment ( R / GCP ) region was studied by pulsed - field gel electrophoresis in 14 of these patients , and we did not find any fragment size difference between the patients and normal individuals who have the same number of pigment genes . 
The R / GCP region was also analyzed in 29 French and seven North American <mark>ALD</mark> patients by using six genomic DNA probes , isolated from a cosmid walk , that flank the color vision genes . 
No deletions were found with probes that lie 3 of the green pigment genes . 
One of the eight previously reported <mark>ALD</mark> individuals has a long deletion 5 of the red pigment gene , a deletion causing blue cone monochromacy . 
This finding and the previous findings of a 45 % frequency of phenotypic color vision defects in patients with <mark>AMN</mark> may suggest that the <mark>ALD</mark> / <mark>AMN</mark> gene lies 5 to the red pigment gene and that the frequent phenotypic <mark>color vision anomalies</mark> owe their origin to deleted DNA that includes regulatory genes for color vision . 
It is possible , however , that phenotypic <mark>color vision anomalies</mark> in <mark>AMN</mark> may be phenocopies secondary to retinal or neural involvement by the disease . 
The single case of blue cone monochromacy may therefore be a fortuitous coincidence of two diseases . . 
<mark>Paroxysmal nocturnal haemoglobinuria</mark> with coexisting <mark>deficiency of the ninth component of complement</mark> : lack of massive <mark>haemolytic attack</mark> . 
A 47 - year - old woman with <mark>paroxysmal nocturnal haemoglobinuria</mark> ( <mark>PNH</mark> ) was found to have an <mark>inherited deficiency in the ninth complement component</mark> ( C9 ) . 
In complement - sensitivity lysis tests , 80 % of her erythrocytes were markedly complement - sensitive ( PNH - III ) . 
Laser cytofluorimetry with a monoclonal antibody against decay - accelerating factor ( DAF ) revealed that 95 % of her erythrocytes were DAF - negative . 
Surprisingly , she has suffered only mild <mark>haemolysis</mark> and has never experienced massive spontaneous <mark>haemolysis</mark> . 
Gross <mark>haemoglobinuria</mark> and <mark>jaundice</mark> occurred only after receiving postoperative transfusion of whole blood . 
In her serum , C9 was not detectable either by immunological or by functional assays . 
Both the Ham test and the sugar water test using normal human serum or plasma yielded marked haemolysis of the patients erythrocytes . 
When the patients serum or plasma was used , only a trace of lysis was detected . 
Addition of purified human C9 to her plasma fully restored haemolysis . 
These observations indicated that C9 may play a critical role in <mark>haemolytic attacks</mark> in patients with <mark>PNH</mark> and that characteristic <mark>haemolysis</mark> in <mark>PNH</mark> may be tempered by coexisting <mark>C9 deficiency</mark> . . 
Duplicational mutation at the <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> locus : its frequency , distribution , origin , and phenotypegenotype correlation . 
Partial gene deletion is the major cause of mutation leading to <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) and <mark>Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>BMD</mark> ) . 
Partial gene duplication has also been recognized in a few cases . 
We have conducted a survey for duplication in 72 unrelated nondeletion patients , analyzed by Southern blot hybridization with clones representing the entire <mark>DMD</mark> cDNA . 
With careful quantitative analysis of hybridization band intensity , 10 cases were found to carry a duplication of part of the gene , a frequency of 14 % for nondeletion cases ( 10 / 72 ) , or 6 % for all cases ( 10 / 181 ) . 
The extent of these duplications has been characterized according to the published exon - containing HindIII fragment map , and in six of the 10 duplications a novel restriction fragment that spanned the duplication junction was detected . 
The resulting translational reading frame of mRNA has been predicted for nine duplications . 
A shift of the reading frame was predicted in four of the six <mark>DMD</mark> cases and in one of the two intermediate cases , while the reading frame remained uninterrupted in both <mark>BMD</mark> cases . 
RFLP and quantitative Southern blot analyses revealed a grandpaternal origin of duplication in four families and grandmaternal origin in one family . 
In all five families , the duplication was found to originate from a single X chromosome . 
Unequal sister - chromatid exchange is proposed to be the mechanism for the formation of these duplications . . 
Glucose 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase variants : Gd ( + ) Alexandra associated with <mark>neonatal jaundice</mark> and Gd ( - ) Camperdown in a young man with <mark>lamellar cataracts</mark> . 
Two male subjects are described , with unusual clinical presentations and with hitherto undescribed G6PD variants . 
The first , of Italian extraction , suffered from severe <mark>neonatal jaundice</mark> following maternal ingestion of fresh broad beans ( Vicia fava ) both prenatally and postnatally the expression of the enzymatic defect was much more severe in the neonatal period than on retesting in adolescence , when biochemical characterization showed unique features which justify designation as a new variant Gd ( + ) Alexandra . 
The second patient , a boy of Maltese extraction who was found to have <mark>bilateral lamellar cataracts</mark> at the age of 4 years , was identified as <mark>G6PD deficient</mark> only as a result of a survey of children of Mediterranean origin with unexplained <mark>cataract</mark> formation ; he has approximately 15 % of normal enzyme activity , with another unique combination of biochemical characteristics which has led to its designation as Gd ( - ) Camperdown . 
Although this association may be coincidental , it prompts further attention to the possibility that under certain circumstances <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> may favor <mark>cataract</mark> formation . 
The two cases illustrate the value of characterization of the mutant enzyme whenever unexpected clinical or laboratory results are obtained . . 
Statistical analysis of the two stage mutation model in <mark>von Hippel - Lindau disease</mark> , and in <mark>sporadic cerebellar haemangioblastoma</mark> and <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> . 
Analysis of the age incidence curves for <mark>unilateral and bilateral retinoblastoma</mark> led Knudson to propose that <mark>hereditary tumours</mark> may arise by a single event and <mark>sporadic tumours</mark> by a two stage mutation process . 
It has been suggested recently that <mark>sporadic renal cell carcinoma</mark> may arise from a two stage mutation process . 
We analysed the age incidence curves for symptomatic <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> ( n = 26 ) and <mark>cerebellar haemangioblastoma</mark> ( n = 68 ) in 109 patients with <mark>von Hippel - Lindau ( VHL ) disease</mark> , and compared them to 104 patients with <mark>sporadic renal cell carcinoma</mark> and 43 patients with <mark>sporadic cerebellar haemangioblastoma</mark> . 
The age incidence curves for <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> and <mark>cerebellar haemangioblastoma</mark> in <mark>VHL disease</mark> were compatible with a single mutation model , whereas the age incidence curves for <mark>sporadic renal cell carcinoma</mark> and <mark>cerebellar haemangioblastoma</mark> suggested a two stage mutation process . 
These data are compatible with the <mark>VHL</mark> gene functioning as a recessive <mark>tumour</mark> suppressor gene . 
<mark>Sporadic cerebellar haemangioblastoma</mark> and some <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> may arise from somatic mutations inactivating both alleles at the <mark>VHL</mark> locus . . 
Screening for carriers of <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> among Ashkenazi Jews . 
A comparison of DNA - based and enzyme - based tests . 
BACKGROUND AND METHODS . 
The prevention of <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> ( <mark>GM2 gangliosidosis , type 1</mark> ) depends on the identification of carriers of the gene for this <mark>autosomal recessive disorder</mark> . 
We compared the enzyme - based test widely used in screening for <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> with a test based on analysis of DNA . 
We developed methods to detect the three mutations in the HEXA gene that occur with high frequency among Ashkenazi Jews two mutations cause infantile <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> , and the third causes the adult - onset form of the disease . 
DNA segments containing these mutation sites were amplified with the polymerase chain reaction and analyzed for the presence of the mutations . 
RESULTS . 
Among 62 Ashkenazi obligate carriers of <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> , the three specific mutations accounted for all but one of the mutant alleles ( 98 percent ) . 
In 216 Ashkenazi carriers identified by the enzyme test , DNA analysis showed that 177 ( 82 percent ) had one of the identified mutations . 
Of the 177 , 79 percent had the exon 11 insertion mutation , 18 percent had the intron 12 splice - junction mutation , and 3 percent had the less severe exon 7 mutation associated with adult - onset disease . 
The results of the enzyme tests in the 39 subjects ( 18 percent ) who were defined as carriers but in whom DNA analysis did not identify a mutant allele were probably false positive ( although there remains some possibility of unidentified mutations ) . 
In addition , of 152 persons defined as noncarriers by the enzyme - based test , 1 was identified as a carrier by DNA analysis ( i . e e . , a false negative enzyme - test result ) . 
CONCLUSIONS . 
The increased specificity and predictive value of the DNA - based test make it a useful adjunct to the diagnostic tests currently used to screen for carriers of <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> . 
<mark>Total deficiency of plasma cholesteryl ester transfer protein</mark> in subjects homozygous and heterozygous for the intron 14 splicing defect . 
The molecular basis of <mark>cholesteryl ester transfer protein ( CETP ) deficiency</mark> was investigated in 4 unrelated <mark>CETP - deficient</mark> families . 
The high density lipoprotein - cholesterol levels of the probands exceeded 150 mg / dl . 
The plasma of the probands was totally deficient in CETP activity and mass . 
The genomic DNA of the patients was amplified by polymerase chain reaction , using two oligonucleotide primers located in the intron 12 and 14 of the CETP gene , and the amplified products were directly sequenced . 
Two patients were homozygous for a G - to - A change at the 5 - splice donor site of the intron 14 . 
The G - to - A change would cause impaired splicing of pre - messenger RNA . 
The other two probands were heterozygous for the mutation , but totally lacked CETP . 
Their lipoprotein patterns were also similar to those of the two homozygotes . 
Thus , other <mark>genetic defects</mark> or metabolic factors influencing CETP expression are implicated . 
The data suggest that the G - to - A mutation may be common in human plasma <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> . 
Furthermore , there could be compound heterozygotes who totally lack plasma CETP and have lipoprotein profiles similar to those of homozygotes . . 
Molecular genetics of the glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) Mediterranean variant and description of a new G6PD mutant , G6PD Andalus1361A . 
<mark>Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ; E . C . 1 . 1 . 1 . 49 ) deficiency</mark> is the most common human <mark>enzymopathy</mark> ; more than 300 different biochemical variants of the enzyme have been described . 
In many parts of the world the Mediterranean type of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> is prevalent . 
However , G6PD Mediterranean has come to be regarded as a generic term applied to similar G6PD mutations thought , however , to represent a somewhat heterogeneous group . 
A C - - - - T mutation at nucleotide 563 of G6PD Mediterranean has been identified by Vulliamy et al . , and the same mutation has been found by De Vita et al . in G6PD Mediterranean , G6PD Sassari , and G6PD Cagliari . 
The latter subjects had an additional mutation , at nucleotide 1311 , that did not produce a coding change . 
We have examined genomic DNA of five patients - - four of Spanish origin and one of Jewish origin - - having enzymatically documented G6PD Mediterranean . 
All had both the mutation at nucleotide 563 and that at nucleotide 1311 . 
A sixth sample , resembling G6PD Mediterranean kinetically but with a slightly rapid electrophoretic mobility , was designated G6PD Andalus and was found to have a different mutation , a G - - - - A transition at nucleotide 1361 , producing an arginine - to - histidine substitution . 
These studies suggest that G6PD Mediterranean is , after all , relatively homogeneous . 
A normal male with an inherited deletion of one exon within the <mark>DMD</mark> gene . 
We describe two brothers with identical inherited deletions of one single exon within the middle of the <mark>DMD</mark> gene ; one brother has <mark>Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> diagnosed at 11 years of age , whereas the older brother is normal at 18 . 
These results have implications for genetic counselling and prenatal diagnosis in families with <mark>Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> . . 
<mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> gene expression in normal and diseased human muscle . 
A probe for the 5 end of the <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) gene was used to study expression of the gene in normal human muscle , myogenic cell cultures , and muscle from patients with <mark>DMD</mark> . 
Expression was found in RNA from normal fetal muscle , adult cardiac and skeletal muscle , and cultured muscle after myoblast fusion . 
In <mark>DMD</mark> muscle , expression of this portion of the gene was also revealed by in situ RNA hybridization , particularly in regenerating muscle fibers . . 
Molecular and phenotypic analysis of patients with deletions within the deletion - rich region of the <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) gene . 
Eighty unrelated individuals with <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) or <mark>Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>BMD</mark> ) were found to have deletions in the major deletion - rich region of the <mark>DMD</mark> locus . 
This region includes the last five exons detected by cDNA5b - 7 , all exons detected by cDNA8 , and the first two exons detected by cDNA9 . 
These 80 individuals account for approximately 75 % of 109 deletions of the gene , detected among 181 patients analyzed with the entire dystrophin cDNA . 
Endpoints for many of these deletions were further characterized using two genomic probes , p20 ( DXS269 ; Wapenaar et al . ) and GMGX11 ( DXS239 ; present paper ) . 
Clinical findings are presented for all 80 patients allowing a correlation of phenotypic severity with the genotype . 
Thirty - eight independent patients were old enough to be classified as <mark>DMD</mark> , <mark>BMD</mark> , or intermediate phenotype and had deletions of exons with sequenced intron / exon boundaries . 
Of these , eight <mark>BMD</mark> patients and one intermediate patient had gene deletions predicted to leave the reading frame intact , while 21 <mark>DMD</mark> patients , 7 intermediate patients , and 1 <mark>BMD</mark> patient had gene deletions predicted to disrupt the reading frame . 
Thus , with two exceptions , frameshift deletions of the gene resulted in more severe phenotype than did in - frame deletions . 
This is in agreement with recent findings by Baumbach et al . and Koenig et al . but is in contrast to findings , by Malhotra et al . at the 5 ' end of the gene . 
Cloning of breakpoints of a chromosome translocation identifies the AN2 locus . 
Chromosome translocations involving 11p13 have been associated with <mark>familial aniridia</mark> in two kindreds highlighting the chromosomal localization of the AN2 locus . 
This locus is also part of the <mark>WAGR</mark> complex ( <mark>Wilms tumor</mark> , <mark>aniridia</mark> , <mark>genitourinary abnormalities</mark> , and <mark>mental retardation</mark> ) . 
In one kindred , the translocation is associated with a deletion , and probes for this region were used to identify and clone the breakpoints of the translocation in the second kindred . 
Comparison of phage restriction maps exclude the presence of any sizable deletion in this case . 
Sequences at the chromosome 11 breakpoint are conserved in multiple species , suggesting that the translocation falls within the AN2 gene . . 
Linkage analysis of the apolipoprotein C2 gene and <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> on human chromosome 19 reveals linkage disequilibrium in a French - Canadian population . 
The gene for human apolipoprotein C2 ( APOC2 ) , situated on the proximal long arm of chromosome 19 , is closely linked to the gene for the most common form of adult <mark>muscular dystrophy</mark> , <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DM</mark> ) . 
Six APOC2 RFLPs ( TaqI , BglI , BanI , BamHI , NcoI , and AvaII ) have been identified to date . 
We have conducted a comprehensive <mark>DM</mark> linkage study utilizing all six RFLPs and involving 50 families and 372 individuals . 
The most informative RFLPs are , in descending order , NcoI ( lod = 6 . 64 , theta = 0 . 05 ) , BglI ( lod = 6 . 12 , theta = 0 . 05 ) , AvaII ( lod = 6 . 02 , theta = 0 . 03 ) , BanI ( lod = 5 . 76 , theta = 0 . 04 ) , TaqI ( lod = 4 . 29 , theta = 0 . 06 ) , and BamHI ( lod = 1 . 75 , theta = 0 . 01 ) . 
A substantial increase in the lod scores over those seen with the individual RFLPs was obtained when the linkage of the entire APOC2 haplotype ( composed of the six RFLPs ) was studied ( lod = 17 . 87 , theta = 0 . 04 ) . 
We have observed significant inter - APOC2 RFLP linkage disequilibrium . 
Consequently , the three most informative RFLPs have been found to be BanI , TaqI , and either BglI , AvaII , or NcoI polymorphisms . 
We also demonstrate linkage disequilibrium between DM and APOC2 in our French - Canadian population ( standardized disequilibrium constant phi = . 22 , chi 2 = 5 . 12 , df = 1 , P less than 0 . 04 ) . 
This represents the first evidence of linkage disequilibrium between APOC2 and the <mark>DM</mark> locus . 
Phenylalanine hydroxylase gene haplotypes in Polynesians : evolutionary origins and absence of alleles associated with severe <mark>phenylketonuria</mark> . 
A total of 630 haplotypes for the phenylalanine hydroxylase ( PAH ) gene locus were established in five groups of Polynesians comprising Samoans , Tongans , Cook Islanders , Maori , and Niueans . 
Considerable genetic continuity was demonstrated between these widely dispersed populations , since three common haplotypes ( 4 , 1 , and 7 ) constituted over 95 % of alleles . 
A control group of individuals from Southeast Asia shared the same major haplotypes , 4 , 1 , and 7 , with Polynesians . 
These data provide further support for the theories of genetic homogeneity and of Asian affinities of the Polynesian precursor populations . 
The absence of severe <mark>phenylketonuria</mark> ( <mark>PKU</mark> ) in both Polynesians and Southeast Asians is consistent with the lack of PAH haplotypes 2 and 3 , on which the severe <mark>PKU</mark> mutants have arisen among Caucasians . . 
Preferential germline mutation of the paternal allele in <mark>retinoblastoma</mark> . 
The event triggering malignant proliferation in 70 % of <mark><mark>retinoblastoma</mark> tumours</mark> is loss of heterozygosity for chromosome 13q14 , whereby the normal retinoblastoma gene ( RB1 ) allele is lost and an already mutated RB1 allele remains in the <mark>tumour</mark> . 
The first allele suffers a mutational event - - deletion , duplication or point mutation ( manuscript in preparation ) - - either in the germ line ( all bilateral patients ) or in a somatic retinal cell ( most unilateral patients ) . 
Most bilateral patients have no family history of <mark>retinoblastoma</mark> and are presumed to have new germline mutations which arose in the egg , sperm or early embryo . 
We have determined the parental origin of the retained allele in nine <mark>retinoblastoma tumours</mark> from eight unrelated non - familial cases by using RB1 - linked genetic markers . 
Six <mark>tumours</mark> retained the paternal allele and three retained the maternal allele . 
Of the three <mark>unilateral tumours</mark> , only one retained the paternal RB1 allele . 
Thus , there is no evidence that the paternal RB1 allele is preferentially retained in <mark>retinoblastoma</mark> , as has been suggested to be the case in <mark>osteosarcoma</mark> . 
By contrast , <mark>tumours</mark> from four of the five bilateral patients retained the paternal RB1 allele . 
This suggests either that new germline RB1 mutations arise more frequently during spermatogenesis than during oogenesis , or that imprinting in the early embryo affects chromosomal susceptibility to mutation . . 
Haplotype analysis of the phenylalanine hydroxylase gene in Turkish <mark>phenylketonuria</mark> families . 
We have estimated the haplotype distribution of mutant and normal phenylalanine hydroxylase ( PAH ) alleles for 17 Turkish <mark>phenylketonuria</mark> ( <mark>PKU</mark> ) families 20 normal and 27 mutated PAH alleles could be identified . 
Of the latter , the most prevalent were associated with haplotype 6 ( 29 . 6 % ) , 1 ( 18 . 5 % ) and 36 ( 11 . 1 % ) , while the normal alleles were preferentially associated with haplotype 1 ( 20 % ) . 
Of the 19 different haplotypes observed , 5 have not been described previously . 
The haplotype distribution differed significantly from that of the Northern European population . 
Two of the eight polymorphic sites were in association with <mark>PKU</mark> . 
No deletions of exon sequences were found in the families analysed . 
<mark>Huntington disease</mark> : no evidence for locus heterogeneity . 
A total of 63 families with <mark>Huntington disease</mark> ( <mark>HD</mark> ) were examined for linkage between <mark>HD</mark> and G8 ( D4S10 ) . 
The families included 57 Caucasian , four Black American , and two Japanese . 
The combined maximum lod score was 87 .

04 ( 99 % confidence interval 0 . 018 - 0 . 071 ) . 
The maximum frequency of recombination was 0 . 
03 in males and 0 . 
05 in females . 
Fifty - seven families gave positive lod scores ; five small families gave mildly negative lod scores . 
The maximum likelihood estimate of alpha , the proportion of linked loci , was 1 . 
0 with a lower 99 % confidence interval of 0 . 
88 . 
These data suggest that there is only one <mark>HD</mark> locus , although a second rare locus cannot be ruled out . 
Haplotype and multipoint linkage analysis in Finnish <mark>choroideremia</mark> families . 
Multipoint linkage analysis of <mark>choroideremia</mark> ( <mark>TCD</mark> ) and seven X chromosomal restriction fragment length polymorphisms ( RFLPs ) was carried out in 18 Finnish <mark>TCD</mark> families . 
The data place <mark>TCD</mark> distal to PGK and DXS72 , very close to DXYS1 and DXYS5 ( Zmax = 24 at theta = 0 ) and proximal to DXYS4 and DXYS12 . 
This agrees with the data obtained from other linkage studies and from physical mapping . 
All the <mark>TCD</mark> males and carrier females studied have the same DXYS1 allele in coupling with <mark>TCD</mark> . 
In Northeastern Finland , 66 / 69 chromosomes carrying <mark>TCD</mark> had the same haplotype at loci DXS72 , DXYS1 , DXYS4 , and DXYS12 . 
The same haplotype is seen in only 15 / 99 chromosomes not carrying <mark>TCD</mark> . 
Moreover , in 71 / 104 non - <mark>TCD</mark> chromosomes , the haplotype at six marker loci is different from those seen in any of the 76 TCD chromosomes . 
This supports the previously described hypothesis that the large Northern Finnish <mark>choroideremia</mark> pedigrees , comprising a total of over 80 living patients representing more than a fifth of all <mark>TCD</mark> patients described worldwide , carry the same mutation . 
These linkage and haplotype data provide improved opportunities for prenatal diagnosis based on RFLP studies . . 
Autosomal dominant <mark>aniridia</mark> linked to the chromosome 11p13 markers catalase and D11S151 in a large Dutch family . 
In a large pedigree with autosomal dominant <mark>aniridia</mark> , we found close linkage between the <mark>aniridia</mark> locus AN2 and the markers catalase ( CAT ) ( zeta = 7 . 27 at theta = 0 . 00 ) and D11S151 ( zeta = 3 . 86 at theta = 0 . 10 ) flanking the AN2 locus on 11p13 . 
Positive lod scores were also obtained for the 11p13 - - - - 11p14 markers D11S16 and FSHB with the linkage group CAT / AN2 / D11S151 . 
We conclude that the autosomal dominant <mark>aniridia</mark> in this family is due to a mutation at the AN2 locus on 11p13 . 
We have excluded linkage ( zeta less than - 2 at theta less than 0 . 18 ) between the <mark>aniridia</mark> and the chromosome 2p25 marker D2S1 ( linked to ACP1 ) . 
Recombination events that locate <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> distal to APOC2 on 19q . 
We previously reported a recombination in an individual with <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DM</mark> ) which placed the markers D19S19 and APOC2 on the same side of the <mark>DM</mark> locus . 
Haplotyping of this family with more recently characterized probes which are either tightly linked to <mark>DM</mark> or distal to the linkage group at q13 . 
2 shows that the <mark>DM</mark> locus is distal to APOC2 . 
This is confirmed by other recombinants where <mark>DM</mark> segregates with distal probes . 
Additional marker to marker recombinations in unaffected individuals are reported and support the order and orientation of the <mark>DM</mark> linkage group as pter - ( INSR , LDLR , S9 ) - ( S19 , BCL3 , APOC2 ) - ( CKMM , DM ) - ( S22 , + + + PRKCG ) - qter . 
The data presented here cannot determine whether <mark>DM</mark> is proximal or distal to CKMM . 
The consequences of this probe order for antenatal diagnosis and future research aiming to isolate the gene which is affected in <mark>DM</mark> are discussed . 
Mutations in the RB1 gene and their effects on transcription . 
Inactivation of both alleles of the RB1 gene during normal retinal development initiates the formation of a <mark>retinoblastoma ( RB ) tumor</mark> . 
To identify the mutations which inactivate RB1 , 21 <mark>RB tumors</mark> isolated from 19 patients were analyzed with the polymerase chain reaction or an RNase protection assay or both . 
Mutations were identified in 13 of 21 <mark>RB tumors</mark> ; in 8 <mark>tumors</mark> , the precise errors in nucleotide sequence were characterized . 
Each of four germ line mutations involved a small deletion or duplication , while three somatic mutations were point mutations leading to splice alterations and loss of an exon from the mature RB1 mRNA . 
We were unable to detect expression of the mutant allele in lymphoblasts of three bilaterally affected patients , although the mutation was present in the genomic DNA and transcripts containing the mutations were obvious in the <mark>RB tumors</mark> in the absence of a normal RB1 allele . 
The variations in the level of expression of mutant transcripts suggest deregulation of RB1 transcription in the absence of a functional RB1 gene product . . 
Partial deletion 8q without <mark>Langer - Giedion syndrome</mark> : a recognisable syndrome . 
We report two de novo cases of del ( 8 ) ( pter - - - - q24 . 1 ) with breakpoints involving the distal part of band 8q24 . 
1 1 . 
The clinical features were similar and there were no obvious stigmata of <mark>Langer - Giedion syndrome</mark> ( <mark>LGS</mark> ) . 
There are three other cases reported with a deletion of chromosome 8 at approximately the same breakpoint , one without <mark>LGS</mark> and some similarities to our cases , the other two with <mark>LGS</mark> . 
Our findings would support the observation that the critical segment for the assignment of <mark>LGS</mark> is proximal to or involves the proximal part of 8q24 . 
1 , but a review of published reports suggests that the aetiology of <mark>LGS</mark> may be a more complex issue

We have studied genetic linkage between the gene for creatine kinase muscle type ( CKMM ) and the gene for <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DM</mark> ) .

Tight linkage was also demonstrated for CKMM and the gene for apolipoprotein C2 ( ApoC2 ) . 
This establishes CKMM as a useful marker for <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> 
<mark>Color vision defects</mark> in <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> . 
The relationship between <mark>abnormal color vision</mark> and <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> ( <mark>AMN</mark> ) was investigated in 27 <mark>AMN</mark> patients and 31 age - matched controls by using the Farnsworth - Munsell 100 Hue test . 
Twelve ( 44 % ) of 27 patients showed test scores significantly above normal . 
The axes of bipolarity determined by the testing differed widely between the patients with abnormal scores , compatible with the notion that different alterations in visual pigment genes occur in different <mark>AMN</mark> kindreds . 
These observations confirm our earlier impression that the frequency of <mark>abnormal color vision</mark> is increased in these kindreds , and it supports our contentions that ( 1 ) <mark>AMN</mark> ( and its companion , <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ) are very closely linked to the visual pigment loci at Xq28 and ( 2 ) this proximity might provide the opportunity to observe <mark>contiguous gene defects</mark> . . 
Molecular analysis of a female <mark>Lesch - Nyhan</mark> patient . 
We report the identification of a female patient with the X - linked recessive <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> ( <mark>hypoxanthine phosphoribosyltransferase [ HPRT ] deficiency</mark> ) . 
Cytogenetic and carrier studies revealed structurally normal chromosomes for this patient and her parents and demonstrated that this mutation arose through a de novo gametic event . 
Comparison of this patients DNA with the DNA of her parents revealed that a microdeletion , which occurred within a maternal gamete and involved the entire HPRT gene , was partially responsible for the disease in this patient . 
Somatic cell hybrids , generated to separate maternal and paternal X chromosomes , showed that expression of two additional X - linked enzymes , phosphoglycerate kinase and glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase , were expressed only in cells that contained the maternal X chromosome , suggesting the presence of a functionally inactive paternal X chromosome . 
Furthermore , comparison of methylation patterns within a region of the HPRT gene known to be important in gene regulation revealed differences between DNA from the father and the patient , in keeping with an active HPRT locus in the father and an inactive HPRT locus in the patient . 
Together these data indicate that nonrandom inactivation of the cytogenetically normal paternal X chromosome and a microdeletion of the HPRT gene on an active maternal X chromosome were responsible for the absence of HPRT in this patient . . 
<mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> : an <mark>X - linked neurologic disorder of myelin metabolism</mark> with a novel mutation in the gene encoding proteolipid protein . 
The nosology of the <mark>inborn errors of myelin metabolism</mark> has been stymied by the lack of molecular genetic analysis . 
Historically , <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> has encompassed a host of <mark>neurologic disorders</mark> that present with a <mark>deficit of myelin</mark> , the membrane elaborated by glial cells that encircles and successively enwraps axons . 
We describe here a <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher</mark> pedigree of the classical type , with X - linked inheritance , a typical clinical progression , and a pathologic loss of myelinating cells and myelin in the central nervous system . 
To discriminate variants of <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> , a set of oligonucleotide primers was constructed to polymerase - chain - reaction ( PCR ) amplify and sequence the gene encoding proteolipid protein ( PLP ) , a structural protein that comprises half of the protein of the myelin sheath . 
The PLP gene in one of two affected males and the carrier mother of this family exhibited a single base difference in the more than 2 kb of the PLP gene sequenced , a C - - - - T transition that would create a serine substitution for proline at the carboxy end of the protein . 
Our results delineate the clinical features of <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> , define the possible molecular pathology of this <mark>dysmyelinating disorder</mark> , and address the molecular classification of <mark>inborn errors of myelin metabolism</mark> . 
Patients with the classical form ( type I ) and the more severely affected , connatal variant of <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease ( type II )</mark> would be predicted to display mutation at the PLP locus . 
The other variants ( types III - VI ) , which have sometimes been categorized as <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> , may represent mutations in genes encoding other structural myelin proteins or proteins critical to myelination . . 
Molecular basis of human <mark><mark>von Willebrand</mark> disease</mark> : analysis of platelet von Willebrand factor mRNA . 
<mark><mark>von Willebrand</mark> disease</mark> ( <mark>vWD</mark> ) , the most common <mark>inherited bleeding disorder</mark> in humans , can result from either a quantitative or a qualitative defect in the adhesive glycoprotein , von Willebrand factor ( vWF ) . 
Molecular studies of <mark>vWD</mark> have been limited by the large size of the vWF gene and difficulty in obtaining the vWF mRNA from patients . 
By use of an adaptation of the polymerase chain reaction , vWF mRNA was amplified and sequenced from peripheral blood platelets . 
A silent vWF allele was identified , resulting from a cis defect in vWF mRNA transcription or processing . 
In two <mark>type IIA vWD</mark> patients , two different but adjacent missense mutations were identified , the locations of which may identify an important vWF functional domain . 
Expression in heterologous cells of recombinant vWF containing one of these latter mutations reproduced the characteristic structural abnormality seen in <mark>type IIA vWD</mark> plasma . . 
<mark>Familial deficiency of the seventh component of complement</mark> associated with recurrent <mark>meningococcal infections</mark> . 
We describe an 11 - year - old girl suffering from <mark>recurrent meningitis</mark> with a complete <mark>absence of the seventh component of complement</mark> ( C7 ) . 
Diagnosis was established by haemolytic titration and western blotting . 
The patients serum lacked the 85 kDa C7 chain . 
Haemolytic activity of serum was reconstituted with either pooled normal human serum or with purified C7 . 
The relatives ( parents and one sister ) had half - normal levels of both immunochemically and functionally determined C7 , indicating a heterozygous state for <mark>C7 deficiency</mark> . . 
Translocation t ( 5 ; 11 ) ( q13 . 1 ; p13 ) associated with familial <mark>isolated aniridia</mark> . 
A father and daughter with <mark>isolated aniridia</mark> were observed to have an apparently balanced , reciprocal translocation involving chromosomes 5 and 11 [ t ( 5 ; 11 ) ( q13 . 1 ; p13 ) ] . 
No other clinical characteristics often associated with the deletion of 11p13 were observed in this family . 
This finding , in association with 3 other instances of single breaks at 11p13 and <mark>aniridia</mark> , supports the assignment of AN2 to 11p13 . 
<mark>Homozygous hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> : a disease distinct from <mark>abetalipoproproteinemia</mark> at the molecular level . 
apoB DNA , RNA , and protein from two patients with <mark>homozygous hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> ( <mark>HBL</mark> ) were evaluated and compared with normal individuals . 
Southern blot analysis with 10 different cDNA probes revealed a normal gene without major insertions , deletions , or rearrangements . 
Northern and slot blot analyses of total liver mRNA from <mark>HBL</mark> patients documented a normal size apoB mRNA that was present in greatly reduced quantities . 
ApoB protein was detected within <mark>HBL</mark> hepatocytes utilizing immunohistochemical techniques ; however , it was markedly reduced in quantity when compared with control samples . 
No apoB was detectable in the plasma of <mark>HBL</mark> individuals with an ELISA assay . 
These data are most consistent with a mutation in the coding portion of the apoB gene in <mark>HBL</mark> patients , leading to an abnormal apoB protein and apoB mRNA instability . 
These results are distinct from those previously noted in <mark>abetalipoproteinemia</mark> , which was characterized by an elevated level of hepatic apoB mRNA and accumulation of intracellular hepatic apoB protein . . 
Spontaneous reversion of novel <mark>Lesch - Nyhan</mark> mutation by HPRT gene rearrangement . 
Molecular analysis of an unusual patient with the <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> has suggested that the mutation is due to a partial HPRT gene duplication . 
We now report the cloning and sequencing of the mutant HPRT cDNA which shows the precise duplication of exons 2 and 3 . 
This mutation is the result of an internal duplication of 16 - 20 kilobases of the gene . 
The structure of the mutant gene suggests that the duplication was not generated by a single unequal crossing - over event between two normal HPRT alleles . 
Growth of <mark>Epstein - Barr</mark> virus - transformed lymphoblasts from this patient in selective medium has permitted isolation of spontaneous HPRT + revertants of this mutation . 
The reversion event involves a second major HPRT gene rearrangement where most or all of the duplicated portion of the mutant gene is deleted . 
The original mutation therefore has the potential for spontaneous somatic reversion . 
This may explain the relatively mild symptoms of the <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> exhibited by this patient . . 
<mark>Complex glycerol kinase deficiency</mark> : molecular - genetic , cytogenetic , and clinical studies of five Japanese patients . 
Five male Japanese patients with <mark>complex glycerol kinase deficiency</mark> ( <mark>CGKD</mark> ) and their relatives were studied clinically , cytogenetically , and molecular - genetically .

Although the deletion differed in size among patients , a segment commonly absent was located between the genomic sequences corresponding to L1 - 4 and cDMD13 - 14 . 
This finding indicated that the gene coding for glycerol kinase ( GK ) is located within this segment . 
A comparison of the clinical manifestations of the present five patients and reported <mark>CGKD</mark> or <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) patients with DNA deletion suggests the existence of a certain gene responsible for <mark>gonadotropin deficiency</mark> ( <mark>GTD</mark> ) .

Genetically determined low C4 : a predisposing factor to <mark>autoimmune chronic active hepatitis</mark> . 
Of 26 patients with <mark>autoimmune chronic active hepatitis</mark> ( <mark>CAH</mark> ) starting in childhood 18 ( 69 % ) had low C4 and 5 ( 19 % ) had low C3 serum levels . 
Impaired hepatic synthesis and immune - consumption were unlikely since transferrin levels were normal in all patients , albumin levels were persistently low in only 3 , and only 3 had raised levels of activation fragment C3d . 
C4d was normal in all patients studied . 
In the families of 12 probands with low C4 , 7 parents had low C4 and 2 had levels which were at the lower limit of normal . 
5 of 10 siblings from 5 families had low C4 . 
These results suggest that low C4 levels in <mark>CAH</mark> are genetically determined . 
C4 phenotyping in 20 patients and in 26 parents showed that 90 % and 81 % , respectively , had null allotypes at either the C4A or C4B locus compared with 59 % in controls , indicating that defective expression of structural genes may contribute to the observed <mark>C4 deficiency</mark> . . 
An amino - acid substitution involved in <mark>phenylketonuria</mark> is in linkage disequilibrium with DNA haplotype 2 . 
<mark>Phenylketonuria</mark> ( <mark>PKU</mark> ) is an <mark>autosomal recessive human genetic disorder</mark> caused by a <mark>deficiency of hepatic phenylalanine hydroxylase</mark> ( PAH , phenylalanine 4 - monooxygenase , EC 1 . 14 . 16 . 1 ) . 
<mark>PKU</mark> is a common <mark>inborn error of amino - acid metabolism</mark> in caucasian populations and approximately 1 in 50 individuals are carriers of a <mark>PKU</mark> allele . 
To define the molecular basis of <mark>PKU</mark> , we characterized twelve restriction fragment - length polymorphism ( RFLP ) haplotypes of the PAH locus in the northern European population and observed that 90 % of the <mark>PKU</mark> alleles in this population are confined to four common RFLP haplotypes . 
We have recently reported a splicing mutation in the PAH gene that is associated with RFLP haplotype 3 which is present at about 40 % of mutant alleles . 
We now report the <mark>molecular lesion</mark> associated with the RFLP haplotype 2 mutant allele . 
This defect is caused by a C - to - T transition in exon 12 resulting in an amino - acid substitution ( Arg to Trp ) at residue 408 of PAH . 
Direct hybridization analysis of the point mutation using a specific oligonucleotide probe demonstrated that this mutation is also in linkage disequilibrium with RFLP haplotype 2 alleles that make up about 20 % of mutant PAH genes 
<mark>Choroideremia</mark> : close linkage to DXYS1 and DXYS12 demonstrated by segregation analysis and historical - genealogical evidence . 
Linkage studies using restriction fragment length polymorphisms were conducted in the <mark>X - linked disorder</mark> , <mark>choroideremia</mark> , designated <mark>TCD</mark> for <mark>Progressive Tapeto - Choroidal Dystrophy</mark> . 
Previously demonstrated close linkage with locus DXYS1 was confirmed ( lod 11 . 44 at 0 recombination distance ) . 
In addition , locus DXYS12 was found to be closely linked with <mark>TCD</mark> ( lod 3 . 31 at 0 recombination distance ) . 
The disease mainly occurs in three large kindreds in remote Northern Finland . 
While formal genealogical proof is lacking , all presently living ( more than 80 affected males and 120 carrier females ) probably originate from a common founder couple born in 1644 and 1646 , twelve generations ago . 
All 36 patients and 48 carriers tested from the three kindreds had the same haplotype ( <mark>TCD</mark> / DXYS1 , 11kb / DXYS12 , 1 . 6kb ) . 
Given that at least 105 female meioses transmitting <mark>TCD</mark> have occurred since 1650 in these kindreds , extremely close linkage between <mark>TCD</mark> , DXYS1 and DXYS12 is suggested . 
The above haplotype is a very useful diagnostic tool in these <mark>TCD</mark> families . 
We suggest that our historical - genealogical approach to linkage analysis may be possible elsewhere in similar isolated populations 
<mark>Von Hippel - Lindau disease</mark> maps to the region of chromosome 3 associated with <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> . 
<mark>Von Hippel - Lindau disease</mark> ( <mark>VHL</mark> ) is an <mark>autosomal dominant disorder</mark> with inherited susceptibility to various forms of <mark>cancer</mark> , including <mark>hemangioblastomas</mark> of the central nervous system , <mark>phaeochromocytomas</mark> , <mark>pancreatic malignancies</mark> , and <mark>renal cell carcinomas</mark> . 
<mark>Renal cell carcinomas</mark> constitute a particularly frequent cause of death in this disorder , occurring as <mark>bilateral and multifocal tumours</mark> , and presenting at an earlier age than in sporadic , non - familial cases of this <mark>tumour</mark> type . 
We report here that the <mark>VHL</mark> gene is linked to the locus encoding the human homologoue of the RAF1 oncogene , which maps to chromosome 3p25 ( ref . 4 ) . 
Crossovers with the <mark>VHL</mark> locus suggest that the defect responsible for the <mark>VHL</mark> phenotype is not a mutation in the RAF1 gene itself . 
An alternative or prior event to oncogene activation in <mark>tumour</mark> formation may be the inactivation of a putative <mark>tumour</mark> suppressor which can be associated with both the <mark>inherited and sporadic forms of the cancer</mark> . 
<mark>Sporadic renal cell carcinomas</mark> have previously been associated with the loss of regions on chromosome 3p ( refs 5 , 6 ) . 
Consequently , sporadic and VHL - associated forms of <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> might both result from alterations causing loss of function of the same <mark>tumour</mark> suppressor gene on this chromosome . . 
Tightly linked flanking markers for the <mark>Lowe oculocerebrorenal syndrome</mark> , with application to carrier assessment . 
The <mark>Lowe oculocerebrorenal syndrome</mark> ( <mark>OCRL</mark> ) is characterized by congenital <mark>cataract</mark> , <mark>mental retardation</mark> , and <mark>defective renal tubular function</mark> .

We have used the Xq25 breakpoint in this patient to determine the position of OCRL relative to the two linked markers .
