Utilization of purines by an HPRT variant in an intelligent , nonmutilative patient with features of the <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> . 
The patient , H . 
Chr . 
B . , was among the first reported with <mark>hyperuricemia</mark> and <mark>central nervous system symptoms</mark> . 
He has been found to have a variant of hypoxanthine guanine phosphoribosyl transferase ( HPRT ; E . C . 2 . 4 . 2 . 8 ) distinct from the enzyme present in patients with the <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> . 
The patient had <mark>chroeoathetosis</mark> , <mark>spasticity</mark> , <mark>dysarthric speech</mark> , and <mark>hyperuricemia</mark> . 
However , his intelligence was normal and he had no evidence of self - mutilation . 
There was no activity of HPRT in the lysates of erythrocytes and cultured fibroblasts when analyzed in the usual manner . 
Using a newly developed method for the study of purine metabolism in intact cultured cells , this patient was found to metabolize some 9 % of 8 - 14C - hypoxanthine , and 90 % of the isotope utilized was converted to adenine and guanine nucleotides . 
In contrast , cells from patients with the <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> were virtually completely unable to convert hypoxanthine to nucleotides . 
The patients fibroblasts were even more efficient in the metabolism of 8 - 14C - guanine , which was utilized to the extent of 27 % , over 80 % of which was converted to guanine and adenine nucleotides . 
The growth of the cultured fibroblasts of this patient was intermediate in media containing hypoxanthine aminopterin thymidine ( HAT ) , whereas the growth of <mark>Lesch - Nyhan</mark> cells was inhibited and normal cells grew normally . 
Similarly in 8 - azaguanine , 6 - thioguanine , and 8 - azahypoxanthine , the growth of the patients cells was intermediate between normal and <mark>Lesch - Nyhan</mark> cells . 
These observations provide further evidence for genetic heterogeneity among patients with disorders in purine metabolism involving the HPRT gene . 
They document that this famous patient did not have the <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> 
Localisation of the <mark>Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> gene on the short arm of the X chromosome by linkage to cloned DNA sequences . 
A linkage study in 30 <mark>Becker muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>BMD</mark> ) kindreds using three cloned DNA sequences from the X chromosome which demonstrate restriction fragment length polymorphisms ( RFLPs ) , suggests that the <mark>BMD</mark> gene is located on the short arm of the X chromosome , in the p21 region . 
The genes for <mark>Becker and Duchenne dystrophies</mark> must therefore be closely linked , if not allelic , and any future DNA probes found to be of practical use in one disorder should be equally applicable to the other . 
The linkage analysis also provides data on the frequency of recombination along the short arm of the X chromosome , and across the centromeric region . . 
Molecular evidence for new mutation at the hprt locus in <mark>Lesch - Nyhan</mark> patients . 
Hypoxanthine - guanine phosphoribosyltransferase ( HPRT ; EC2 . 4 . 2 . 8 ) , which functions in the metabolic salvage of purines , is encoded by an X - linked gene in man . 
Partial <mark>HPRT deficiencies</mark> are associated with <mark>gouty arthritis</mark> , while absence of activity results in <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> ( <mark>L - N</mark> ) . 
<mark>L - N</mark> patients fail to reproduce and the heterozygous state appears to confer no selective advantage . 
Thus , Haldanes principle predicts that new mutations at the hprt locus must occur frequently in order for <mark>L - N syndrome</mark> to be maintained in the population . 
This constant introduction of new mutations would be expected to result in a heterogeneous collection of <mark>genetic lesions</mark> , some of which may be novel . 
As we report here , the mutations in the hprt gene of seven <mark>L - N</mark> patients , selected from an initial survey of 28 patients , have been characterized and all were found to be distinctly different , as predicted . 
The origin of one unusual mutation has been identified by analysis of DNA from four generations of family members . 
Further molecular analysis of the origin of new mutations at the hprt locus should aid in resolving the issue of an apparent difference in the frequency of hprt mutations in males and females 
Allelic exclusion of glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase in platelets and T lymphocytes from a <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> carrier . 
An obligate carrier of the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> ( <mark>WAS</mark> ) who was also heterozygous for the A and B types of X - linked glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase was found . 
With her it became possible to determine whether allelic exclusion occurs in particular cell - types of the <mark>WAS</mark> carrier . 
If so , the remaining cells of a particular cell - type would express only the normal X chromosome and only one glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase isoenzyme would be demonstrable . 
This carrier had only the B isoenzyme of glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase in platelets and thymus - derived T lymphocytes , although both isoenzymes A and B were present in erythrocytes and neutrophils . 
These findings suggest that selection against the <mark>WAS</mark> gene occurs in platelets and thymus - derived T lymphocytes and that the defects associated with <mark>WAS</mark> expressed in these cell - types may be implicated in the genesis of the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> . . 
<mark>Complement deficiency</mark> and <mark>nephritis</mark> . 
A report of a family . 
A family is described in which three children had homozygous <mark>deficiency of C3</mark> and in which both parents and two other children were heterozygous for the C3 null gene . 
One child with heterozygous <mark>C3 deficiency</mark> was found to have membranoproliferative <mark>glomerulonephritis</mark> ; <mark>proteinuria</mark> and / or microscopical <mark>haematuria</mark> was present in all three homozygous <mark>C3 - deficient</mark> children . 
All children with homozygous or heterozygous <mark>C3 deficiency</mark> were , to a varying degree , susceptible to infection . 
The only child of the family with normal complement had no increased risk of infection and no <mark>renal disease</mark> . 
This family study provides further support for the proposal that <mark>C3 deficiency</mark> predisposes to <mark>nephritis</mark> . . 
Heterogeneity of <mark>glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase deficiency</mark> in Algeria . 
Study in Northern Algeria with description of five new variants . 
<mark>Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) deficiency</mark> was found in 3 . 
2 % of the male population living in the urban area of Algiers . 
The deficient subjects originated from multiple geographic regions of Northern Algeria , with prevalence of individuals of Berber - Kabyle origin . 
Red blood cell G6PD was partially purified and characterized in deficient males from 17 families , and six different variants were found . 
Among them , only one , the Gd ( - ) Kabyle variant , had been previously described . 
It was detected in nine families . 
The other five variants were new Gd ( - ) Laghouat ( four cases ) , Gd ( - ) Blida ( one case ) , Gd ( - ) Thenia ( one case ) , Gd ( - ) Titteri ( one case ) , and Gd ( - ) Alger ( two brothers ) . 
Strikingly , the common Mediterranean variant was not found . 
<mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> is heterogeneous in northern Algeria where autochtonous variants seem to prevail . 
The Kabyle variant may be common in this country . 
<mark>Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase deficiency</mark> inhibits in vitro growth of Plasmodium falciparum . 
<mark>Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ; EC 1 . 1 . 1 . 49 ) - deficient</mark> red blood cells from male hemizygotes and female heterozygotes from the island of Sardinia were studied for their ability to support growth in vitro of the <mark>malaria</mark> - causing organism Plasmodium falciparum . 
Parasite growth was approximately one - third of normal in both hemi - and heterozygotes for <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> . 
In Sardinians with the beta 0 - <mark>thalassemia</mark> trait , parasite growth was normal except when <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> occurred together with the thalassemia trait . 
The data support the hypothesis that <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> may confer a selective advantage in a <mark>malarious</mark> area ; the female heterozygote may be at a particular advantage because resistance to <mark>malaria</mark> equals that of male hemizygotes , but the risk of <mark>fatal hemolysis</mark> may be less . 
However , more female heterozygotes must be studied to confirm this hypothesis . 
No protective effect of beta 0 - thalassemia trait could be demonstrated in vitro . 
Bone marrow transplant in <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> . 
An allogeneic bone marrow transplant ( BMT ) from a normal HLA identical sibling donor was performed in a 13 - year - old boy with rapidly progressive <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) . 
Engraftment and complete hematologic recovery occurred within 4 weeks , but <mark>neurologic deterioration</mark> continued . 
The patient died of an <mark>adenovirus infection</mark> 141 days after BMT . 
<mark>ALD</mark> is characterized by abnormally high plasma levels of very long chain fatty acids ( VLCFA ) as a result of impaired capacity to degrade them . 
Ten days after BMT , the white blood cell VLCFA levels and enzyme activity became normal ; after 3 months , there was progressive reduction of plasma VLCFA to levels only slightly above normal . . 
[ Gd - allele distribution patterns in Azerbaijan . III . The identification of mutant forms of glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ] 
In 28 families with <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> living in 3 settlements of Shekii district of Azerbaijan 11 G6PD variants of II and III classes differing by kinetic properties were identified according WHO program . 
9 of them are characterized with the same electrophoretic mobility . 
Comparison of G6PD spectra in two subpopulations and in a mixed group permits to make a conclusion about existence of common and rare G6PD alleles in examined population . 
They distribute by gene drift supported by natural selection . 
Among 7 samples of G6PD with normal and increased activity two new variants of IV class - - Nukha and Bash - Kungut - - were found . . 
<mark>Adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> : survey of 303 cases : biochemistry , diagnosis , and therapy . 
<mark>Adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) is a genetically determined disorder associated with <mark>progressive central demyelination</mark> and <mark>adrenal cortical insufficiency</mark> . 
All affected persons show increased levels of saturated unbranched very - long - chain fatty acids , particularly hexacosanoate ( C26 0 ) , because of impaired capacity to degrade these acids . 
This degradation normally takes place in a subcellular organelle called the peroxisome , and <mark>ALD</mark> , together with <mark>Zellwegers cerebrohepatorenal syndrome</mark> , is now considered to belong to the newly formed category of <mark>peroxisomal disorders</mark> . 
Biochemical assays permit prenatal diagnosis , as well as identification of most heterozygotes . 
We have identified 303 patients with <mark>ALD</mark> in 217 kindreds . 
These patients show a wide phenotypic variation . 
Sixty percent of patients had childhood <mark>ALD</mark> and 17 % <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> , both of which are X - linked , with the gene mapped to Xq28 . 
<mark>Neonatal ALD</mark> , a distinct entity with autosomal recessive inheritance and points of resemblance to <mark>Zellwegers syndrome</mark> , accounted for 7 % of the cases . 
Although excess C26 0 in the brain of patients with <mark>ALD</mark> is partially of dietary origin , dietary C26 0 restriction did not produce clear benefit . 
Bone marrow transplant lowered the plasma C26 0 level but failed to arrest neurological progression . . 
Genetic polymorphism of G6PD in a Bulgarian population . 
Considerable genetic heterogeneity in G6PD was found in the Bulgarian population - 14 G6PD variants isolated from 117 hemizygous carriers of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> . 
Of these , G6PD Mediterranean type was a polymorphic variant and G6PD Corinth occurred with high frequency . 
Two new variants were identified - G6PD Rudosem and G6PD Nedelino . 
In a selected group of 78 subjects with clinical manifestations , four variants were established G6PD Mediterranian , G6PD Corinth , G6PD Seattle and G6PD Ohut II . . 
Clinical use of DNA markers linked to the gene for <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> . 
Seventy families with <mark>Duchenne muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DMD</mark> ) known to the Institute of Child Health fall into three categories with respect to potential linkage analysis with the X chromosome DNA markers RC8 and L1 . 
28 that bridge the <mark>DMD</mark> gene . 
Families in which there is at least one obligatory female heterozygote ( n = 13 ) . 
Here prediction and exclusion of <mark>DMD</mark> gene transmission may be possible , the accuracy being dependent on the closeness of the linkage of the DNA marker ( s ) to the <mark>DMD</mark> gene ; an illustrative case is reported . 
Families in which there is a single affected boy , who also has one or more healthy brothers ( n = 26 ) . 
Given an informative restriction fragment length polymorphism ( RFLP ) , the probability that the boy represents a new mutation can be reassessed ; it is also possible to exclude the <mark>DMD</mark> gene in a sister . 
Families with a single affected boy with no brother ( n = 30 ) . 
Here exclusion of the <mark>DMD</mark> gene in a sister may be possible . 
Only in one family was there no possibility of useful linkage analysis . 
The linkage analysis required is described , and the need to check <mark>DMD</mark> families for informative RFLPs is stressed . 
Family studies in <mark>Bechterew ' s syndrome</mark> ( <mark>ankylosing spondylitis</mark> ) III . 
Genetics . 
The results of segregation analyses in 75 families where the proband had <mark>ankylosing spondylitis</mark> , are presented . 
Of the 278 adult , living first degree relatives , approximately 85 % cooperated in the study . 
Clinical and radiographical examinations were performed and HLA typing was conducted . 
The results were in agreement with our hypothesis that <mark>ankylosing spondylitis</mark> is part of a syndrome where different genetic factors interact . 
Such known factors are HLA B27 associated disease susceptibility , susceptibility to <mark>psoriatic arthropathy</mark> and susceptibility to <mark>entero - arthropathy</mark> . 
Radiographical <mark>sacro - iliitis</mark> was restricted to HLA B27 positive relatives , and was more frequently found in relatives to probands with <mark>psoriasis</mark> than in relatives to probands without <mark>psoriasis</mark> . 
Environmental factors ( intestinal bacteria ) are known to trigger the disease at least in some persons , and we have postulated that all or most of them have the predisposition to develop disease . 
Thus , the syndrome has a multifactorial etiology . 
The phenotypic expressions of the different genetic predispositions involved , include <mark>sacro - iliitis</mark> , <mark>psoriasis</mark> , <mark>acute anterior uveitis</mark> , peripheral <mark>arthropathy</mark> and <mark>inflammatory bowel disease</mark> . 
We suggest the descriptive name <mark>HEREDITARY MULTIFOCAL RELAPSING INFLAMMATION</mark> ( <mark>HEMRI</mark> ) for this syndrome . 
<mark>Ankylosing spondylitis</mark> , <mark>psoriatic arthropathy</mark> and <mark>entero - arthropathy</mark> may be regarded as clinical sub - types of the syndrome . . 
<mark>Prader - Willi syndrome</mark> and chromosome 15 . 
A clinical discussion of 20 cases . 
A <mark>chromosome 15 anomaly</mark> was observed in 12 of 20 patients , 17 of whom were clinically suspected of having <mark>Prader - Willi syndrome</mark> ( <mark>PWS</mark> ) . 
The clinical features of eight cases with 15q11 - 12 deletion were very similar to those originally described in <mark>PWS</mark> . 
On the other hand , the group of normal karyotype patients is heterogeneous , and their features do not strictly correspond to the clinical definition of <mark>PWS</mark> . 
However , the hypothesis that <mark>PWS</mark> is associated with deletion of 15q11 - 12 can neither explain the apparently balanced translocations of chromosome 15 nor account for the small supernumerary metacentric chromosomes corresponding to an isochromosome 15 for band 15q11 observed in some cases . . 
The <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> gene in North American Jewish populations : geographic variations and origin . 
From data collected in a North American <mark>Tay - Sachs disease</mark> ( <mark>TSD</mark> ) heterozygote screening program , the <mark>TSD</mark> carrier frequency among 46 , 304 Jewish individuals was found to be . 
0324 ( 1 in 31 individuals ) . 
This frequency is consistent with earlier estimates based on <mark>TSD</mark> incidence data . 
<mark>TSD</mark> carrier frequencies were then examined by single country and single region of origin in 28 , 029 Jews within this sample for whom such data were available for analysis . 
Jews with Polish and / or Russian ancestry constituted 88 % of this sample and had a <mark>TSD</mark> carrier frequency of . 
0327 . 
No <mark>TSD</mark> carriers were observed among the 166 Jews of Near Eastern origins . 
Relative to Jews of Polish and Russian origins , there was at least a twofold increase in the <mark>TSD</mark> carrier frequency in Jews of Austrian , Hungarian , and Czechoslovakian origins ( P less than . 005 ) . 
These findings suggest that the <mark>TSD</mark> gene proliferated among the antecedents of modern Ashkenazi Jewry after the Second Diaspora ( 70 A . D . ) and before their major migrations to regions of Poland and Russia ( before 1100 A . D . ) . 
Human <mark>deficiency of the sixth component of complement</mark> in a patient with <mark>meningococcal meningitis</mark> and no <mark>haemostasis abnormality</mark> . 
A case of human complete <mark>C6 deficiency</mark> is reported . 
The patient , a 31 year old white male , was seen on the occasion of an isolated episode of <mark>meningococcal meningitis</mark> . 
Serum complement hemolytic and bactericidal activities were lacking and could be restored to normal by addition of appropriate amounts of purified C6 . 
No <mark>hemostatic abnormalities</mark> were observed . . 
<mark>Absence of the seventh component of complement</mark> in a patient with <mark>chronic meningococcemia</mark> presenting as <mark>vasculitis</mark> . 
A previously healthy 40 - year - old man presenting with <mark>fever</mark> , <mark>arthritis</mark> , and <mark>cutaneous vasculitis</mark> was found to have <mark>chronic meningococcemia</mark> . 
Evaluation of his complement system showed an absence of functional and antigenic C7 , compatible with a complete <mark>deficiency of the seventh component of complement</mark> . 
Study of the patients family spanning four generations showed heterozygous <mark>deficiency of C7</mark> in five members . 
<mark>Chronic neisserial infection</mark> can be associated with <mark>C7 deficiency</mark> and must be distinguished from other causes of <mark>cutaneous vasculitis</mark> . . 
<mark>Familial discoid lupus erythematosus</mark> associated with heterozygote <mark>C2 deficiency</mark> . 
Two siblings with <mark>chronic discoid lupus erythematosus</mark> and several family members were found with heterozygous <mark>C2 deficiency</mark> . 
An association with histocompatibility markers HLA - B18 and HLA - Dw2 was demonstrated , and the slow allotype of factor B was present . 
Linkage studies in this family suggested a close linkage between the <mark>C2 deficiency</mark> gene and genes coding for B18 , Dw2 , and BfS antigens . 
One HLA - ACB / DBf recombinant was observed showing closer linkage between HLA - D and Bf than between HLA - B and Bf . . 
<mark>Severe - glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) deficiency</mark> associated with chronic <mark>hemolytic anemia</mark> , <mark>granulocyte dysfunction</mark> , and increased susceptibility to infections : description of a new molecular variant ( G6PD Barcelona ) . 
Molecular , kinetic , and functional studies were carried out on erythrocytes and leukocytes in a Spanish male with <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> , <mark>congenital nonspherocytic hemolytic anemia</mark> ( <mark>CNSHA</mark> ) , and increased susceptibility to infections . 
G6PD activity was absent in patients red cells and was about 2 % of normal in leukocytes . 
Molecular studies using standard methods ( WHO , 1967 ) showed G6PD in the patient to have a slightly fast electrophoretic mobility at pH 8 . 
0 with otherwise normal properties ( heat stability at 46 degrees C , apparent affinity for substrates , optimum pH , and utilization of substrate analogues ) . 
Other tests showed the patients granulocytes to engulf latex particles normally , but to have impaired reduction of nitroblue tetrazolium and ferricytochrome - c as well as reduced iodination . 
Chemotaxis and random migration of the patients granulocytes were normal as were myeloperoxidase , leukocyte alkaline phosphatase ( LAP ) , and ultrastructural features . 
The molecular characteristics of G6PD in the patient differed from those of all previously reported variants associated with <mark>CNSHA</mark> , so the present variant was provisionally called G6PD Barcelona to distinguish it from other G6PD variants previously described . 
Possible mechanisms for the severe <mark>deficiency of G6PD</mark> in erythrocytes and granulocytes was investigated by studies on the immunologic specific activity of the mutant enzyme . 
<mark>Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase deficiency</mark> in Papua New Guinea . 
The description of 13 new variants . 
A total of 362 males from various regions of Papua New Guinea were screened for red cell glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) activity . 
Twenty - six <mark>G6PD deficient</mark> individuals were identified . 
Biochemical characterization of G6PD purified from these subjects has revealed 13 new variants and several copies of previously described forms of G6PD . 
This study illustrates the extreme heterogeneity of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> among the people of Papua New Guinea . . 
Heterogeneity of " Mediterranean type " <mark>glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) deficiency</mark> in Spain and description of two new variants associated with <mark>favism</mark> . 
Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) ; EC 1 . 
1 . 
1 . 
49 from thirty - six unrelated Spanish males was partially purified from blood , and the variants were characterized biochemically and electrophoretically according to the methods recommended by the world Health Organization . 
Subjects were from multiple geographic regions within Spain , and all suffered from <mark>hemolytic anemia</mark> , either acute ( 34 cases ) or chronic nonspherocytic ( 2 cases ) . 
Almost all the variants studied presented residual erythrocyte G6PD activity ranging from 0 to 10 % of normal , and five different mutants were responsible for the deficient phenotype . 
Three variants were similar to others previously described G6PD Mediterranean ( 11 cases ) , G6PD Athens - like ( 3 cases ) , and G6PD Union ( 2 cases ) . 
The remaining variants were different from the numerous variants already reported and have been considered as new mutants . 
Provisionally they are called G6PD Betica ( 19 cases ) and G6PD Menorca ( 1 case ) . 
The present study constitutes the first attempt to characterize the <mark>deficient G6PD</mark> variants found in Spain and supplies new data on the relationship between molecular characteristics of deficient variants and their clinical manifestations . 
The most important findings can be summarized as follows ( 1 ) The Spanish population is characterized by an important heterogeneity in <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> . 
( 2 ) Although G6PD Mediterranean is very frequent , it presents a relatively high degree of polymorphism . 
( 3 ) <mark>Favism</mark> has been observed associated with all kinds of variants described here . 
( 4 ) G6PD Betica , which is the most frequent variant found in subjects of Southern Spanish origin , has been observed associated with <mark>favism</mark> in all cases except one . 
A new glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase variant ( G6PD Nagano ) associated with <mark>congenital hemolytic anemia</mark> . 
A new glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) variant associated with <mark>chronic nonspherocytic hemolytic anemia</mark> was reported . 
The patient , a 6 - year - old Japanese male , was noticed to have <mark>hemolytic anemia</mark> soon after birth , and a diagnosis of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> was made at the age of 2 . 
He had episodes of <mark>hemolytic crisis</mark> several times after <mark>upper respiratory infection</mark> . 
G6PD activity of the patient was 5 . 
5 % of normal . 
The enzymatic characteristics were examined when he was 5 years old , and his G6PD showed faster - than - normal electrophoretic mobility , low Km G6P , high Km NADP , low Ki NADPH , normal utilization of substrate analogues , heat instability , and a normal pH optimum curve . 
From these results , this was considered to be a new variant and was designated G6PD Nagano . 
Infection - induced <mark>hemolysis</mark> and <mark>chronic hemolytic anemia</mark> seem to be due to markedly impaired enzyme activity and thermal instability . 
Heterozygous <mark>C2 - deficiency</mark> and <mark>myasthenia gravis</mark> . 
<mark>Complement deficiency</mark> states in <mark>myasthenia gravis</mark> ( <mark>MG</mark> ) have not been reported previously . 
We describe a 19 - year - old woman with typical <mark>MG</mark> and heterozygous <mark>C2 deficiency</mark> , along with HLA typing of the patient and her immediate family . . 
<mark>Adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> : increased plasma content of saturated very long chain fatty acids . 
With a new method we measured the saturated very long chain fatty acids in the plasma of <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) hemizygotes , <mark>ALD</mark> heterozygotes , and controls . 
<mark>ALD</mark> hemizygotes showed increased levels of hexacosanoate ( C26 fatty acid ) which represented 0 .

C25 , C24 , and C23 fatty acids were also increased , but the C22 and C20 fatty acids were normal . 
C26 levels were also increased in most <mark>ALD</mark> heterozygotes , with a mean level 0 . 
057 + / - 0 . 
0063 % of total fatty acids . 
The technique can be used for diagnosis and carrier identification , and in the evaluation of therapy . 
Abnormal high density lipoproteins in <mark>cerebrotendinous xanthomatosis</mark> . 
The plasma lipoprotein profiles and high density lipoproteins ( HDL ) were characterized in patients with the <mark>genetic disease</mark> <mark>cerebrotendinous xanthomatosis</mark> ( <mark>CTX</mark> ) . 
<mark>Abnormalities in the HDL</mark> may contribute to their increased atherogenesis and excessive deposits of tissue sterols in the presence of low or low - normal concentrations of plasma cholesterol ( 165 + / - 25 mg / dl ) and low density lipoproteins ( LDL ) . 
The mean HDL - cholesterol concentration in the <mark>CTX</mark> plasmas was 14 . 
5 + / - 3 . 
2 mg / dl , about one - third the normal value . 
The low HDL - cholesterol reflects a low concentration and an abnormal lipid composition of the plasma HDL . 
Relative to normal HDL , the cholesteryl esters are low , free cholesterol and phospholipids essentially normal , and triglycerides increased . 
The ratio of apoprotein ( apo ) to total cholesterol in the HDL of <mark>CTX</mark> was two to three times greater than normal . 
In the <mark>CTX</mark> HDL , the ratio of apoAI to apoAII was high , the proportion of apoC low , and a normally minor form of apoAI increased relative to other forms . 
The HDL in electron micrographs appeared normal morphologically and in particle size . 
The abnormalities in lipoprotein distribution profile and composition of the plasma HDL result from metabolic defects that are not understood but may be linked to the <mark>genetic defect</mark> in bile acid synthesis in <mark>CTX</mark> . 
As a consequence , it is probable that the normal functions of the HDL , possibly including modulation of LDL - cholesterol uptake and the removal of excess cholesterol from peripheral tissues , are perturbed significantly in this disease . 
Genetics of <mark>cerebrotendinous xanthomatosis</mark> ( <mark>CTX</mark> ) : an autosomal recessive trait with high gene frequency in Sephardim of Moroccan origin . 
We described 6 patients ( from 3 families ) affected with <mark>cerebrotendinous xanthomatosis</mark> ( <mark>CTX</mark> ) . 
All are Sephardic Jews of Moroccan extraction . 
In view of the small number of <mark>CTX</mark> patients diagnosed in the world ( a total of 50 including our 6 patients ) , we are probably dealing with an ethnic subgroup with a high CTX gene frequency , which we have estimated to be 1 / 108 . 
Since there are differences in expression in this disease , we recommend cholestanol study in cases of undiagnosed <mark>cataract</mark> or <mark>tendinous xanthomas</mark> in childhood or early adolescence . 
The diagnosis in <mark>CTX</mark> is important not only for genetic counseling , but also in veiw of possible treatment . . 
New genetic variants of glucose 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) in Italy . 
Six new variants of human erythrocyte G6PD have been characterized . 
All of them were found in Italian males and all were associated with <mark>enzyme deficiency</mark> , but only two with signs of <mark>haemolysis</mark> . 
These and other variants reported in the literature , which must thus far be regarded as sporadic , are found to map in parts of Italy where common types of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> are also prevalent . . 
Variants of erythrocyte glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) in Bulgarian populations . 
Ten variants of erythrocyte glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase were identified in 22 patients with <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> from three districts of Bulgaria . 
Corinth - like and Fayoum - like variants were the most frequent ; Mediterranean , Ohut II , Kilgore , Boston , Poznan , and Panay variants and two new variants , Petrich and Gotze Delchev , were each found in one or two carriers . 
No correlation was revealed between clinical and biochemical polymorphism . . 
<mark>Nephropathy</mark> in the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> . 
<mark>Nephropathy</mark> was detected in five of 32 patients with the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> who were participating in a study of transfer factor ( TF ) therapy . 
In two patients , <mark>nephropathy</mark> was present before TF and did not appear changed by TF therapy . 
One of these patients subsequently developed progressive <mark>renal failure</mark> requiring dialysis beginning 5 1 / 2 years after TF therapy . 
In two patients , decreased renal function appeared very soon after the administration of TF . 
One patient showed gradually decreasing renal function beginning after two years of TF therapy . 
An additional patient was identified who died with <mark>renal failure</mark> without having received TF . 
The results suggest that <mark>renal failure</mark> occurs in the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> more frequently than generally recognized and that administration of TF may precipitate or accelerate the <mark>renal disease</mark> in patients with this syndrome . . 
<mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> : cellular impairments and their implication for carrier detection . 
A family in which two male siblings were affected with <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> ( <mark>WAS</mark> ) was studied using G - 6 - PD isoenzymes as an X - linked marker in order to investigate the nature of cellular abnormalities . 
Isolated peripheral blood cell types from the doubly heterozygous mother of the affected males seemingly failed to express the G - 6 - PD allele in cis position with the <mark>WAS</mark> allele while her cultured skin fibroblasts expressed both G - 6 - PD alleles . 
Additionally , a histogram analysis of platelet size revealed a single population of abnormally small platelets in the affected propositus , whereas the heterozygous mother had no appreciable small platelet subpopulation . 
In vitro culture of hemopoietic progenitor cells of the heterozygous mother showed that the majority of progenitor cells did not express the <mark>WAS</mark> allele . 
However , a small number of cells expressing the G - 6 - PD type linked with the <mark>WAS</mark> allele were detected . 
The proportion of the latter progenitors was significantly higher among more primitive progenitors ( those giving rise to later appearing colonies ) . 
This observation suggests that selection against cells expressing the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich defect</mark> takes place in the hemopoietic system of the heterozygous female and offers a possible means of carrier detection in some women . 
Linkage studies in this family revealed one example of probable recombination between the loci for <mark>WAS</mark> and G - 6 - PD among three informative subjects , suggesting that these two loci may not be closely linked on the X - chromosome . . 
A new CT pattern in <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> . 
A new CT pattern was observed in 2 patients with <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) . 
This pattern , which the authors call Type II , is characterized by the absence of posterior periventricular areas of decreased attenuation around the trigone on non - contrast scans after contrast infusion , however , there is striking enhancement of various white - matter structures ( tracts or fiber systems ) such as the internal capsules , corpus callosum , corona radiata , forceps major , and cerebral peduncles . 
This is different from numerous previous descriptions of the CT pattern in <mark>ALD</mark> . 
<mark>Type II ALD</mark> does not appear to have been seen in any other <mark>leukoencephalopathy</mark> and is probably specific for a phenotypic variant or an evolving stage of <mark>ALD</mark> . . 
Further evidence for heterogeneity of <mark>glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase deficiency</mark> in Papua New Guinea . 
Four new G6PD variants have been characterized in individuals from Papua New Guinea . 
This study demonstrates that the previously reported Markham variant and the newly characterized Salata variant may be widely distributed in Papua New Guinea . 
Th data presented here together with those of previously published studies demonstrate a degree of heterogeneity of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> that is much higher than that in other regions of the world where <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> is common . . 
Increased incidence of <mark>cataracts</mark> in male subjects <mark>deficient in glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase</mark> . 
<mark>Glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) deficiency</mark> in RBCs was found significantly more frequently in 210 male <mark>cataractous</mark> patients than in 672 control subjects of Sardinian origin . 
The frequency of the deficiency was increasingly higher in presenile <mark>cataracts</mark> . 
In the <mark>G6PD - deficient</mark> group , the incidence of <mark>cortical and total cataracts</mark> was also increased . 
It is suggested that decrease of the G6PD activity in the lens , which accompanies its deficiency in the erythrocyte , might play a role in the cataracto - genesis of these patients . 
Moreover , <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> should be added to other conditions , such as the <mark>galactosemic</mark> states and <mark>riboflavin deficiency</mark> , where <mark>cataracts</mark> represent a sensitive indicator of <mark>metabolic abnormalities</mark> of the RBC . . 
Molecular basis of human mitochondrial <mark>very - long - chain acyl - CoA dehydrogenase deficiency</mark> causing <mark>cardiomyopathy</mark> and <mark>sudden death</mark> in childhood . 
beta - Oxidation of long - chain fatty acids provides the major source of energy in the heart . 
Defects in enzymes of the beta - oxidation pathway cause <mark>sudden , unexplained death</mark> in childhood , acute <mark>hepatic encephalopathy</mark> or <mark>liver failure</mark> , <mark>skeletal myopathy</mark> , and <mark>cardiomyopathy</mark> . 
Very - long - chain acyl - CoA dehydrogenase [ VLCAD ; very - long - chain - acyl - CoA ( acceptor ) 2 , 3 - oxidoreductase , EC 1 . 3 3 . 99 99 . 13 ] catalyzes the first step in beta - oxidation . 
We have isolated the human VLCAD cDNA and gene and determined the complete nucleotide sequences . 
Polymerase chain reaction amplification of VLCAD mRNA and genomic exons defined the molecular defects in two patients with <mark>VLCAD deficiency</mark> who presented with unexplained <mark>cardiac arrest</mark> and <mark>cardiomyopathy</mark> . 
In one , a homozygous mutation in the consensus dinucleotide of the donor splice site ( g + 1 - - > a ) was associated with universal skipping of the prior exon ( exon 11 ) . 
The second patient was a compound heterozygote , with a missense mutation , C1837 - - > T , changing the arginine at residue 613 to tryptophan on one allele and a single base deletion at the intron - exon 6 boundary as the second mutation . 
This initial delineation of human mutations in VLCAD suggests that <mark>VLCAD deficiency</mark> reduces myocardial fatty acid beta - oxidation and energy production and is associated with <mark>cardiomyopathy</mark> and <mark>sudden death</mark> in childhood . 
Aberrant subcellular localization of BRCA1 in <mark>breast cancer</mark> . 
The BRCA1 gene product was identified as a 220 - kilodalton nuclear phosphoprotein in normal cells , including breast ductal epithelial cells , and in 18 of 20 <mark>tumor</mark> cell lines derived from tissues other than breast and ovary . 
In 16 of 17 <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> lines and 17 of 17 samples of cells obtained from malignant effusions , however , BRCA1 localized mainly in cytoplasm . 
Absence of BRCA1 or aberrant subcellular location was also observed to a variable extent in histological sections of many <mark>breast cancer</mark> biopsies . 
These findings suggest that <mark>BRCA1 abnormalities</mark> may be involved in the pathogenesis of many <mark>breast cancers</mark> , sporadic as well as familial . . 
Mapping of the mouse homologue of the <mark>Wilson disease</mark> gene to mouse chromosome 8 . 
ATP7B , the gene altered in <mark>Wilson disease</mark> ( <mark>WD</mark> ) patients , lies in a block of homology shared between human chromosome 13q14 and the central region of mouse chromosome 14 . 
However , we have mapped the murine homologue of ATP7B ( Atp7b ) to mouse chromosome 8 by somatic cell hybrid analysis . 
Analysis of 80 interspecific backcross offspring was used to position Atp7b close to D8Mit3 and another ATPase locus , Atp4b , on mouse chromosome 8 . 
ATP4B lies in 13q34 and is separated from ATP7B by several loci whose mouse homologues map to mouse chromosome 14 . 
The assignment of Atp7b to mouse chromosome 8 identifies a previously unrecognized region of homology between this chromosome and human chromosome 13 . 
This assignment suggests a possible location for the toxic milk mutation in the mouse , which has been proposed as a homologue of <mark>WD</mark> . . 
Germline mutations of the BRCA1 gene in <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> families provide evidence for a genotype - phenotype correlation . 
Mutations in the BRCA1 gene , discovered in 1994 , are associated with an 80 - 90 % lifetime risk of <mark>breast cancer</mark> . 
We have analysed 60 families with a history of <mark>breast and / or ovarian cancer</mark> for germline mutations in BRCA1 . 
Twenty - two different mutations were detected in 32 families ( 53 % ) , of which 14 are previously unreported . 
We observed a significant correlation between the location of the mutation in the gene and the ratio of <mark>breast to ovarian cancer</mark> incidence within each family . 
Our data suggest a transition in risk such that mutations in the 3 third of the gene are associated with a lower proportion of <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> . 
Haplotype analysis supports previous data which suggest some BRCA1 mutation carriers have common ancestors ; however , we have found at least two examples where recurrent mutations appear to have arisen independently . . 
Hereditary <mark>deficiency of the seventh component of complement</mark> and recurrent <mark>meningococcal infection</mark> : investigations of an Irish family using a novel haemolytic screening assay for complement activity and C7 M / N allotyping . 
<mark>Terminal complement component deficiency</mark> predisposes to <mark>meningococcal infection</mark> and is inherited in an autosomal co - dominant manner . 
An Irish family is described , in which 2 of 3 brothers had recurrent <mark>meningococcal infection</mark> . 
A novel screening assay was used to investigate for <mark>terminal complement deficiency</mark> and the 2 affected brothers were found to be <mark>completely deficient in the seventh component of complement</mark> ( C7 ) . 
Enzyme - linked immunosorbent assay for C7 revealed lower than normal levels in the remaining brother and parents . 
C7 M / N protein polymorphism allotyping , used to investigate the segregation of the <mark>C7 deficiency</mark> genes , showed that the apparently complement sufficient brother was heterozygous <mark>C7 deficient</mark> and a carrier of one of the deficiency genes . 
Complement screening should be carried out in any individual suffering recurrent <mark><mark>meningococcal</mark> infection</mark> or infection with an uncommon meningococcal serogroup . 
Identification of <mark>complement deficient</mark> patients allows the implementation of strategies to prevent recurrent infection . . 
Molecular basis of <mark>subtotal complement C6 deficiency</mark> . 
A carboxy - terminally truncated but functionally active C6 . 
Individuals with <mark>subtotal complement C6 deficiency</mark> possess a C6 molecule that is 14 % shorter than normal C6 and present in low but detectable concentrations ( 1 - 2 % of the normal mean ) . 
We now show that this dysmorphic C6 is bactericidally active and lacks an epitope that was mapped to the most carboxy - terminal part of C6 using C6 cDNA fragments expressed as fusion proteins in the pUEX expression system . 
We thus predicted that the abnormal C6 molecule might be carboxy - terminally truncated and sought a mutation in an area approximately 14 % from the carboxy - terminal end of the coding sequence . 
By sequencing PCR - amplified products from this region , we found , in three individuals from two families , a mutation that might plausibly be responsible for the defect . 
All three have an abnormal 5 splice donor site of intron 15 , which would probably prevent splicing . 
An in - frame stop codon is found 17 codons downstream from the intron boundary , which would lead to a truncated polypeptide 13 . 
5 % smaller than normal C6 . 
This result was unexpected , as earlier studies mapped the C5b binding site , or a putative enzymatic region , to this part of C6 . 
Interestingly , all three subjects were probably heterozygous for both <mark>subtotal C6 and complete C6 deficiency</mark> . 
<mark>Myotonic dystrophy</mark> : evidence for a possible dominant - negative RNA mutation . 
The trinucleotide expansion mutation causing <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> is in the 3 untranslated region of a protein kinase gene . 
The molecular mechanisms by which the expanded repeat causes the clinically variable and <mark>multisystemic disease</mark> , <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> , are not understood . 
It has been particularly difficult to rationalize the dominant inheritance with the fact that the expansion mutation lies outside of the protein - encoding gene elements , and should not be translated into protein . 
Here we use muscle biopsies from classical adult - onset <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> patients to study the accumulation of transcripts from both the normal and expanded <mark>DM</mark> kinase genes in patient muscle , and compare the results to normal and <mark>myopathic</mark> controls . 
We found relatively small decreases of <mark>DM</mark> kinase RNA in the total RNA pool from muscle ; however , these reductions were not disease specific . 
Analysis of poly ( A ) + RNA showed dramatic decreases of both the mutant and normal <mark>DM</mark> kinase RNAs , and these changes were disease - specific . 
Our findings are consistent with a novel molecular pathogenetic mechanism for <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> both the normal and expanded <mark>DM</mark> kinase genes are transcribed in patient muscle , but the abnormal expansion - containing RNA has a dominant effect on RNA metabolism by preventing the accumulation of poly ( A ) + RNA . 
The ability of the expansion mutation to alter accumulation of poly ( A ) + RNA in trans suggests that <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> may be the first example of a dominant - negative mutation manifested at the RNA level . . 
A strong candidate for the <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> susceptibility gene BRCA1 . 
A strong candidate for the 17q - linked BRCA1 gene , which influences susceptibility to <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> , has been identified by positional cloning methods . 
Probable predisposing mutations have been detected in five of eight kindreds presumed to segregate BRCA1 susceptibility alleles . 
The mutations include an 11 - base pair deletion , a 1 - base pair insertion , a stop codon , a missense substitution , and an inferred regulatory mutation . 
The BRCA1 gene is expressed in numerous tissues , including breast and ovary , and encodes a predicted protein of 1863 amino acids . 
This protein contains a zinc finger domain in its amino - terminal region , but is otherwise unrelated to previously described proteins . 
Identification of BRCA1 should facilitate early diagnosis of <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> susceptibility in some individuals as well as a better understanding of <mark>breast cancer</mark> biology . . 
Molecular characterization of <mark>galactosemia</mark> ( type 1 ) mutations in Japanese . 
We characterized two novel mutations of the galactose - 1 - phosphate uridyltransferase ( GALT ) gene in two Japanese patients with <mark>GALT deficiency</mark> and identified N314D and R333W mutations , previously found in Caucasians . 
One novel missense mutation was an G - to - A transition in exon 8 , resulting in the substitution of arginine by histidine at the codon 231 ( R231H ) . 
GALT activity of the R231H mutant construct was reduced to 15 % of normal controls in a COS cell expression system . 
The other was a splicing mutation , an A - to - G transition at the 38th nucleotide in exon 3 ( 318A - - > G ) , resulting in a 38 - bp deletion in the GALT cDNA by activating a cryptic splice acceptor site . 
In seven Japanese families ( 14 alleles for classic form and one allele for Duarte variant ) with <mark>GALT deficiency</mark> , the R231H and 318A - - > G mutations were found only on both alleles of the proband . 
The N314D and R333W mutations were found on one allele each . 
The Q188R was prevalent in the United States but not in Japanese patients . 
The N314D mutation was associated with the Duarte variant in Japanese persons , as well as in the United States . 
We speculate that <mark>classic galactosemia</mark> mutations appear to differ between Japanese and Caucasian patients . 
Our limited data set on <mark>galactosemia</mark> mutations in Japanese suggests that the N314D GALT mutation encoding the Duarte variant arose before Asian and Caucasian people diverged and that <mark>classic galactosemia</mark> mutations arose and / or accumulated after the divergence of Asian and Caucasian populations . . 
Three novel <mark>aniridia</mark> mutations in the human PAX6 gene . 
<mark>Aniridia</mark> ( <mark>iris hypoplasia</mark> ) is an <mark>autosomal dominant congenital disorder of the eye</mark> . 
Mutations in the human <mark>aniridia</mark> ( PAX6 ) gene have now been identified in many patients from various ethnic groups . 
In the study reported here we describe PAX6 mutations in one sporadic and five familial cases with <mark>aniridia</mark> . 
Of the four different mutations identified , one was identical to a previously reported mutation ( C - - > T transition at codon 240 ) , and three were novel two in the glycine - rich region and one in the proline / serine / threonine - rich ( PST ) region . 
One PAX6 mutation found in the PST region was associated with <mark>cataracts</mark> in an <mark>aniridia</mark> family . 
Another splice mutation in the PST domain occurred in an <mark>aniridia</mark> patient with <mark>anosmia</mark> ( inability to smell ) . 
The six new <mark>aniridia</mark> cases reported here have mutations predicted to generate incomplete PAX6 proteins . 
These results support the theory that human <mark>aniridia</mark> is caused by <mark>haploinsufficiency of PAX6</mark> . . 
The carrier frequency of the BRCA1 185delAG mutation is approximately 1 percent in Ashkenazi Jewish individuals . 
Since BRCA1 , the first major gene responsible for <mark>inherited breast cancer</mark> , was cloned , more than 50 unique mutations have been detected in the germline of individuals with <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> . 
In high - risk pedigrees , female carriers of BRCA1 mutations have an 80 - 90 % lifetime risk of <mark>breast cancer</mark> , and a 40 - 50 % risk of <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> . 
However , the mutation stats of individuals unselected for <mark>breast or ovarian cancer</mark> has not been determined , and it is not known whether mutations in such individuals confer the same risk of <mark>cancer</mark> as in individuals from the high - risk families studied so far . 
Following the finding of a 185delAG frameshift mutation in several Ashkenazi Jewish breast / ovarian families , we have determined the frequency of this mutation in 858 Ashkenazim seeking genetic testing for conditions unrelated to <mark>cancer</mark> , and in 815 reference individuals not selected for ethnic origin . 
We observed the 185delAG mutation in 0 . 
9 % of Ashkenazim ( 95 % confidence limit , 0 . 4 - 1 . 8 % ) and in none of the reference samples . 
Our results suggest that one in a hundred women of Ashkenazi descent may be at especially high risk of developing <mark>breast and / or ovarian cancer</mark> . 
Identification and localization of huntingtin in brain and human lymphoblastoid cell lines with anti - fusion protein antibodies . 
The <mark>Huntington disease</mark> ( <mark>HD</mark> ) phenotype is associated with expansion of a trinucleotide repeat in the IT15 gene , which is predicted to encode a 348 - kDa protein named huntington . 
We used polyclonal and monoclonal anti - fusion protein antibodies to identify native huntingtin in rat , monkey , and human . 
Western blots revealed a protein with the expected molecular weight which is present in the soluble fraction of rat and monkey brain tissues and lymphoblastoid cells from control cases . 
In lymphoblastoid cell lines from juvenile - onset heterozygote <mark>HD</mark> cases , both normal and mutant huntingtin are expressed , and increasing repeat expansion leads to lower levels of the mutant protein . 
Immunocytochemistry indicates that huntingtin is located in neurons throughout the brain , with the highest levels evident in larger neurons . 
In the human striatum , huntingtin is enriched in a patch - like distribution , potentially corresponding to the first areas affected in <mark>HD</mark> . 
Subcellular localization of huntingtin is consistent with a cytosolic protein primarily found in somatodendritic regions . 
Huntingtin appears to particularly associate with microtubules , although some is also associated with synaptic vesicles . 
On the basis of the localization of huntingtin in association with microtubules , we speculate that the mutation impairs the cytoskeletal anchoring or transport of mitochondria , vesicles , or other organelles or molecules . . 
Marked phenotypic heterogeneity associated with expansion of a CAG repeat sequence at the <mark>spinocerebellar ataxia 3 / Machado - Joseph disease</mark> locus . 
The <mark>spinocerebellar ataxia 3</mark> locus ( <mark>SCA3</mark> ) for <mark>type I autosomal dominant cerebellar ataxia</mark> ( <mark>ADCA type I</mark> ) , a clinically and genetically heterogeneous group of <mark>neurodegenerative disorders</mark> , has been mapped to chromosome 14q32 . 
1 1 . 
<mark>ADCA type I</mark> patients from families segregating <mark>SCA3</mark> share clinical features in common with those with <mark>Machado - Joseph disease</mark> ( <mark>MJD</mark> ) , the gene of which maps to the same region . 
We show here that the disease gene segregating in each of three French <mark>ADCA type I</mark> kindreds and in a French family with neuropathological findings suggesting the ataxochoreic form of <mark>dentatorubropallidoluysian atrophy</mark> carries an expanded CAG repeat sequence located at the same locus as that for <mark>MJD</mark> . 
Analysis of the mutation in these families shows a strong negative correlation between size of the expanded CAG repeat and age at onset of clinical disease . 
Instability of the expanded triplet repeat was not found to be affected by sex of the parent transmitting the mutation . 
Evidence was found for somatic and gonadal mosaicism for alleles carrying expanded trinucleotide repeats . 
Overexpression of DM20 messenger RNA in two brothers with <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> . 
<mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> is a <mark>rare , sex - linked recessive , dysmyelinating disease of the central nervous system</mark> that has been associated with mutations in the myelin proteolipid protein ( PLP ) gene . 
Only 25 % of patients studied with <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> have exonic mutations in this gene , the underlying cause of the disease in the remaining patients is unknown . 
The PLP gene encodes two major alternatively spliced transcripts called PLP and DM20 . 
PLP messenger RNA is specifically expressed in central nervous system tissue , whereas DM20 messenger RNA is found in central nervous system , cardiac , and other tissues . 
We studied cultured skin fibroblasts from 2 brothers with <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> who exhibited no detectable exonic mutation of the PLP gene . 
Examination of RNA from these cells showed that the level of DM20 messenger RNA is elevated sixfold relative to male control skin fibroblasts . 
An unrelated female carrier , also with no detectable exonic mutation , showed a threefold increase in DM20 messenger RNA in cultured skin fibroblasts . 
Our findings suggest that in some patients , <mark>Pelizaeus - Merzbacher disease</mark> is caused by overexpression of PLP gene transcripts , and that in these families a 50 % increase of DM20 messenger RNA in females , relative to the increase in affected males , can identify a female carrier . . 
The <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> and <mark>X - linked congenital thrombocytopenia</mark> are caused by mutations of the same gene . 
The <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> ( <mark>WAS</mark> ) is an <mark>X - linked recessive disorder</mark> characterized by <mark>thrombocytopenia</mark> , small platelets , <mark>eczema</mark> , recurrent infections , and <mark>immunodeficiency</mark> . 
Besides the classic <mark>WAS</mark> phenotype , there is a group of patients with <mark>congenital X - linked thrombocytopenia</mark> ( <mark>XLT</mark> ) who have small platelets but only transient <mark>eczema</mark> , if any , and minimal <mark>immune deficiency</mark> . 
Because the gene responsible for <mark>WAS</mark> has been sequenced , it was possible to correlate the <mark>WAS</mark> phenotypes with <mark>WAS</mark> gene mutations . 
Using a fingerprinting screening technique , we determined the approximate location of the mutation in 13 unrelated <mark>WAS</mark> patients with mild to severe clinical symptoms . 
Direct sequence analysis of cDNA and genomic DNA obtained from patient - derived cell lines showed 12 unique mutations distributed throughout the <mark>WAS</mark> gene , including insertions , deletions , and point mutations resulting in amino acid substitutions , termination , exon skipping , or splicing defects . 
Of 4 unrelated patients with the <mark>XLT</mark> phenotype , 3 had missense mutations affecting exon 2 and 1 had a splice - site mutation affecting exon 9 . 
Patients with classic <mark>WAS</mark> had more complex mutations , resulting in termination codons , frameshift , and early termination . 
These findings provide direct evidence that <mark>XLT</mark> and <mark>WAS</mark> are caused by mutations of the same gene and suggest that severe clinical phenotypes are associated with complex mutations . . 
<mark>Myotonia levior</mark> is a <mark>chloride channel disorder</mark> . 
The group of <mark>dominant non - dystrophic myotonias</mark> , comprising disorders characterized by clinically similar forms of myogenic muscle stiffness , is genetically inhomogeneous . 
<mark>Dominant myotonia congenita</mark> ( <mark>Thomsens disease</mark> ) is linked to CLCN1 , the gene encoding the major muscle chloride channel , localized on chromosome 7q35 . 
In contrast , <mark>dominant myotonias</mark> sensitive to potassium are caused by point mutations in SCN4A on chromosome 17q , the gene for the alpha subunit of the adult skeletal muscle sodium channel . 
No linkage or molecular genetic data are as yet available on <mark><mark>myotonia</mark> levior</mark> characterized by milder symptoms and later onset of myotonia than in <mark>Thomsens disease</mark> , and absence of <mark>muscle hypertrophy</mark> . 
We report a CLCN1 Gln - 552 - Arg substitution for a family with dominant inheritance previously diagnosed to have <mark>myotonia levior</mark> . 
Thus , this disorder appears as a variant of <mark>Thomsens disease</mark> due to mutations leading to low clinical expressivity . 
In addition , we report a novel Ile - 290 - Met CLCN1 mutation for a typical Thomsen pedigree . 
In another family previously diagnosed as having <mark>Thomsens disease</mark> , we unexpectedly found a CLCN1 14 bp deletion known to cause <mark>recessive myotonia</mark> , and a rare Trp - 118 - Gly polymorphism . . 
Southern analysis reveals a large deletion at the hypoxanthine phosphoribosyltransferase locus in a patient with <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> . 
Whole genomic hprt clones were used in Southern analysis to screen the integrity of the hprt gene in a family that includes a patient with <mark>HPRT enzyme deficiency</mark> causal to <mark>Lesch - Nyhan syndrome</mark> . 
A 5 kb DNA sequence deletion was found to have its endpoints in the first and third introns . 
The probes identified the carrier status of female family members , aided by an RFLP carried by the mothers normal X - chromosome . . 
Characterisation of molecular defects in <mark>X - linked amelogenesis imperfecta</mark> ( AIH1 ) . 
Amelogenins are an heterogenous family of proteins produced by ameloblasts of the enamel organ during tooth development . 
Disturbances of enamel formation occur in <mark>amelogenesis imperfecta</mark> , a clinically heterogenous group of <mark>inherited disorders</mark> characterised by defective enamel biomineralisation . 
An amelogenin gene , AMGX , has been mapped to the short of the X chromosome ( Xp22 . 1 - p22 . 3 ) and has been implicated in the molecular pathology of <mark>X - linked amelogenesis imperfecta</mark> ( <mark>AIH1</mark> ) . 
We have identified three families exhibiting <mark>AIH1</mark> and screened the AMGX gene for mutations using single - strand conformational polymorphism analysis and DNA sequencing . 
Three novel mutations were identified a C - T substitution in exon 5 , and a G - T substitution and single cytosine deletion in exon 6 , confirming the existence of extensive allelic heterogeneity in this condition . 
The identification of family - specific mutations will enable early identification of affected individuals and correlation of clinical phenotype with genotype will facilitate an objective system of disease classification . 
Frequency of exon 15 missense mutation ( 442D : G ) in cholesteryl ester transfer protein gene in <mark>hyperalphalipoproteinemic</mark> Japanese subjects . 
Cholesteryl ester transfer protein ( CETP ) transfers cholesteryl ester from high density lipoprotein ( HDL ) to apo B - containing lipoproteins . 
The <mark>hyperalphalipoproteinemia</mark> caused by <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> is fairly common in Japan and one of the most common mutations in the CETP gene is the splicing defect of the intron 14 , the allelic frequency of which has been shown to be 0 . 
0049 in the Japanese general population . 
Recently , we have reported a missense mutation in exon 15 of the CETP gene ( 442D G ) , showing a dominant effect on the CETP activity and HDL - cholesterol level . 
In the current study , we determined the frequency of this new mutation in Japanese <mark>hyperalphalipoproteinemic</mark> ( HDL - cholesterol > or = 100 mg / dl ) subjects . 
A rapid and easy screening method for this new mutation was developed using a polymerase chain reaction ( PCR ) - mediated site - directed mutagenesis .

The relative allelic frequency of this mutation was calculated to be 0 . 
17 . 
One of the homozygotes for the 442D G mutation was the patient previously described by us as having <mark>hyperalphalipoproteinemia</mark> with <mark>corneal opacity</mark> and <mark>coronary heart disease</mark> . 
This was the first reported subject homozygous for the <mark>CETP deficiency</mark> who also demonstrated <mark>atherosclerotic symptoms</mark> . 
In homozygous subjects , CETP activity ranged from 37 % to 62 % of the normal value , which was consistent with the results obtained from the transient expression experiment previously reported ; however , the specific activity of CETP was not as low as expected .

<mark>Mucopolysaccharidosis IVA</mark> ( <mark>MPS IVA</mark> ) is an <mark>autosomal recessive disorder</mark> caused by a <mark>deficiency in N - acetylgalactosamine - 6 - sulfatase</mark> ( GALNS ) . 
We found two separate deletions of nearly 8 .

0 kb in the GALNS gene , including some exons . 
There are Alu repetitive elements near the breakpoints of the 8 .

The other 6 .
