Putative <mark>X - linked adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> gene shares unexpected homology with ABC transporters . 
<mark>Adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) is an <mark>X - linked disease</mark> affecting 1 / 20 , 000 males either as <mark>cerebral ALD</mark> in childhood or as <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> ( <mark>AMN</mark> ) in adults . 
Childhood <mark>ALD</mark> is the more severe form , with onset of neurological symptoms between 5 - 12 years of age . 
<mark>Central nervous system demyelination</mark> progresses rapidly and death occurs within a few years . 
<mark>AMN</mark> is a milder form of the disease with onset at 15 - 30 years of age and a more progressive course . 
<mark>Adrenal insufficiency</mark> ( <mark>Addisons disease</mark> ) may remain the only clinical manifestation of <mark>ALD</mark> . 
The principal biochemical abnormality of <mark>ALD</mark> is the accumulation of very - long - chain fatty acids ( VLCFA ) because of impaired beta - oxidation in peroxisomes . 
The normal oxidation of VLCFA - CoA in patients fibroblasts suggested that the gene coding for the VLCFA - CoA synthetase could be a candidate gene for <mark>ALD</mark> . 
Here we use positional cloning to identify a gene partially deleted in 6 of 85 independent patients with <mark>ALD</mark> . 
In familial cases , the deletions segregated with the disease . 
An identical deletion was detected in two brothers presenting with different clinical <mark>ALD</mark> phenotypes . 
Candidate exons were identified by computer analysis of genomic sequences and used to isolate complementary DNAs by exon connection and screening of cDNA libraries . 
The deduced protein sequence shows significant sequence identity to a peroxisomal membrane protein of M ( r ) 70K that is involved in peroxisome biogenesis and belongs to the ATP - binding cassette superfamily of transporters . . 
Targeted modification of the apolipoprotein B gene results in <mark>hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> and <mark>developmental abnormalities</mark> in mice . 
<mark>Familial hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> is an <mark>autosomal codominant disorder</mark> resulting in a dramatic reduction in plasma concentrations of apolipoprotein ( apo ) B , cholesterol , and beta - migrating lipoproteins . 
A benefit of <mark>hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> is that mildly affected individuals may be protected from <mark>coronary vascular disease</mark> . 
We have used gene targeting to generate mice with a modified Apob allele . 
Mice containing this allele display all of the hallmarks of human <mark>hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> they produce a truncated apoB protein , apoB70 , and have markedly decreased plasma concentrations of apoB , beta - lipoproteins , and total cholesterol . 
In addition , the mice manifest several characteristics that are occasionally observed in human <mark>hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> , including reduced plasma triglyceride concentrations , fasting <mark>chylomicronemia</mark> , and reduced high density lipoprotein cholesterol . 
An unexpected finding is that the modified Apob allele is strongly associated with <mark>exencephalus</mark> and <mark>hydrocephalus</mark> . 
These mice should help increase our understanding of <mark>hypobetalipoproteinemia</mark> , <mark>atherogenesis</mark> , and the etiology of <mark>exencephalus</mark> and <mark>hydrocephalus</mark> . . 
A novel disease with <mark>deficiency of mitochondrial very - long - chain acyl - CoA dehydrogenase</mark> . 
Palmitoyl - CoA dehydrogenase activity in skin fibroblasts from seven patients with unidentified defects of fatty acid oxidation was measured in the presence and absence of antibodies against medium - chain , long - chain , and very - long - chain acyl - CoA dehydrogenases ( VLCAD ) . 
Two of the patients , 4 - 5 month old boys , were found to have a novel disease , <mark>VLCAD deficiency</mark> , as judged from the results of very low palmitoyl - CoA dehydrogenase activity and the lack of immunoreactivity toward antibody raised to purified VLCAD . . 
Molecular characterization of <mark>glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) deficiency</mark> in patients of Chinese descent and identification of new base substitutions in the human G6PD gene . 
The underlying DNA changes associated with <mark>glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase ( G6PD ) - deficient</mark> Asians have not been extensively investigated . 
To fill this gap , we sequenced the G6PD gene of 43 <mark>G6PD - deficient</mark> Chinese whose G6PD was well characterized biochemically . 
DNA samples were obtained from peripheral blood of these individuals for sequencing using a direct polymerase chain reaction ( PCR ) sequencing procedure . 
From these 43 samples , we have identified five different types of nucleotide substitutions in the G6PD gene at cDNA 1388 from G to A ( Arg to His ) ; at cDNA 1376 from G to T ( Arg to Leu ) ; at cDNA 1024 from C to T ( Leu to Phe ) ; at cDNA 392 from G to T ( Gly to Val ) ; at cDNA 95 from A to G ( His to Arg ) . 
These five nucleotide substitutions account for over 83 % of our 43 <mark>G6PD - deficient</mark> samples and these substitutions have not been reported in non - Asians . 
The substitutions found at cDNA 392 and cDNA 1024 are new findings . 
The substitutions at cDNA 1376 and 1388 account for over 50 % of the 43 samples examined indicating a high prevalence of these two alleles among <mark>G6PD - deficient</mark> Chinese . 
Our findings add support to the notion that diverse point mutations may account largely for much of the phenotypic heterogeneity of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> . . 
Identification of mutations in Danish <mark>choroideremia</mark> families . 
We have searched for mutations in the <mark>choroideremia</mark> gene ( <mark>CHM</mark> ) in patients from 12 Danish families in which <mark>CHM</mark> is segregating . 
Employing polymerase chain reaction ( PCR ) , single strand conformation polymorphism ( SSCP ) analysis , and direct DNA sequencing , different mutations have been identified in 6 patients . 
All the mutations will interfere with the correct translation of the mRNA predicting a truncated protein or no gene product at all . . 
Structure and genomic sequence of the <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DM</mark> kinase ) gene . 
The mutation causing <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>DM</mark> ) has recently been identified as an unstable CTG trinucleotide repeat located in the 3 untranslated region of a gene encoding for a protein with putative serine - threonine protein kinase activity . 
In this report we present the genomic sequences of the human and murine <mark>DM</mark> kinase gene . 
A comparison of these sequences with each other and with known cDNA sequences from both species , led us to predict a translation initiation codon , as well as determine the organization of the <mark>DM</mark> kinase gene . 
Several polymorphisms within the human <mark>DM</mark> kinase gene have been identified , and PCR assays to detect two of these are described . 
The complete sequence and characterization of the structure of the <mark>DM</mark> kinase gene , as well as the identification of novel polymorphisms within the gene , represent an important step in a further understanding of the genetics of <mark>myotonic dystrophy</mark> and the molecular biology of the gene . . 
Autosomal recessive transmission of <mark>hemophilia A</mark> due to a <mark>von Willebrand</mark> factor mutation . 
The differential diagnosis of the <mark>genetic bleeding disorders</mark> , <mark>hemophilia A</mark> and <mark><mark>von Willebrand</mark> disease</mark> , is occasionally confounded by the close molecular relationship of coagulation factor VIII and von Willebrand factor ( vWF ) . 
This report describes the autosomal inheritance of a <mark>hemophilia A</mark> phenotype due to a mutation of vWF that results in defective factor VIII binding . 
The proband was a female patient with low levels of factor VIII activity . 
Polymerase chain reaction ( PCR ) amplification and DNA sequencing were employed to examine exons encoding the putative factor VIII binding domain of vWF . 
The patient was found to be homozygous for a single point mutation causing a Thr - - > Met substitution at amino acid position 28 in the mature vWF subunit . 
The phenotypic expression of the mutation was determined to be recessive because heterozygous family members were clinically unaffected . 
Recombinant vWF containing the observed amino acid substitution was expressed in COS - 1 cells . 
The mutant vWF was processed and secreted normally , and was functionally equivalent to wild - type vWF in its ability to bind to platelets . 
However , the mutant failed to bind factor VIII , demonstrating that the mutation was functionally related to the observed <mark>hemophilia</mark> phenotype . 
The family we describe demonstrates the recessive inheritance of a recently recognized class of genetic bleeding disorders , we call " autosomal <mark>hemophilia</mark> . 
" We conclude that vWF mutation may be an under recognized cause of <mark>hemophilia</mark> , especially in cases where the inheritance pattern is not consistent with X - linked transmission . 
Somatic <mark>von Hippel - Lindau</mark> mutation in clear cell <mark>papillary cystadenoma of the epididymis</mark> . 
<mark>Papillary cystadenoma of the epididymis</mark> is an uncommon benign lesion that may occur sporadically or as a manifestation of <mark>von Hippel - Lindau ( VHL ) disease</mark> . 
Neither immunohistochemical studies nor molecular genetic analyses of the <mark>VHL</mark> gene have been reported previously for this lesion . 
The authors describe two cases of clear cell <mark>papillary cystadenoma of the epididymis</mark> , both of which were initially confused with <mark>metastatic renal cell carcinoma</mark> . 
Both lesions showed positive immunohistochemical staining for low and intermediate molecular weight keratins ( Cam 5 . 2 and AE1 / AE3 ) , EMA , vimentin , alpha 1 - antitrypsin , and alpha 1 - antichymotrypsin . 
Each was negative for CEA . 
Because clear cell <mark>papillary cystadenoma</mark> is similar to <mark>renal cell carcinoma</mark> histologically , and because both occur as components of the <mark>von Hippel - Lindau disease</mark> complex , the authors analyzed both cases for the presence of mutations in the <mark>VHL</mark> gene . 
A somatic <mark>VHL</mark> gene mutation was detected in one of the two <mark>tumors</mark> by polymerase chain reaction followed by single - strand conformation polymorphism analysis . 
Direct sequencing revealed a cytosine to thymine transition at nucleotide 694 , resulting in the replacement of an arginine with a stop codon after the sixth amino acid of exon 3 . 
As the <mark>VHL</mark> gene is believed to function as a <mark>tumor</mark> suppressor gene , <mark>VHL</mark> gene mutations may play a role in the initiation of tumorigenesis in sporadic <mark>cystadenomas of the epididymis</mark> . 
Identification of WASP mutations in patients with <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> and <mark>isolated thrombocytopenia</mark> reveals allelic heterogeneity at the <mark>WAS</mark> locus . 
Mutation in the gene encoding the recently isolated WASP protein has now been identified as the <mark>genetic defect</mark> responsible for the <mark>X - linked Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> ( <mark>WAS</mark> ) , a primary <mark>immunodeficiency disease</mark> associated with extensive phenotypic variability . 
To elucidate the range of WASP mutations responsible for <mark>WAS</mark> , we used PCR - SSCP analysis to screen for WASP gene mutation in 19 unrelated boys with the diagnosis of classical or attenuated <mark>WAS</mark> or <mark>isolated thrombocytopenia</mark> . 
All 19 patients had WASP mutations , each of which localized to the initial three or terminal three exons of the gene , and the majority of which were unique in each case . 
However , a missense mutation which results in substitution of the arginine at <mark>WAS</mark> codon 86 was identified in three boys with severe <mark>WAS</mark> as well as in one boy presenting with <mark>thrombocytopenia</mark> alone . 
While the three mutations found in the <mark>isolated thrombocytopenia</mark> patients leave the reading frame intact , about one - half of the gene alterations detected in both severe and attenuated <mark>WAS</mark> patients result in frameshifted transcript and premature translation termination . 
These findings therefore confirm the association of <mark>WAS</mark> with WASP mutation and identify WASP mutation as a cause for isolated <mark>congenital thrombocytopenia</mark> in males . 
While the WASP gene defects responsible for <mark>isolated thrombocytopenia</mark> and other mild presentations of <mark>WAS</mark> do not appear distinct from those resulting in severe <mark>WAS</mark> , these data indicate that analysis of WASP gene mutation provides a valuable tool for distinguishing the spectrum of <mark>WAS</mark> patients and the subset of males with <mark>isolated thrombocytopenia</mark> who represent mild cases of <mark>WAS</mark> . . 
WASP gene mutations in <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> and <mark>X - linked thrombocytopenia</mark> . 
The WASP gene has been recently cloned from Xp11 . 
23 and shown to be mutated in three patients with the <mark>Wiskott - Aldrich syndrome</mark> ( <mark>WAS</mark> ) . 
We have developed a screening protocol for identifying WASP gene alterations in genomic DNA and have identified a spectrum of novel mutations in 12 additional unrelated families . 
These missense , nonsense and frameshift mutations involve eight of the 12 exons of the gene . 
Two mutations creating premature termination codons were associated with lack of detectable mRNA on Northern blots . 
Four amino acid substitutions , Leu27Phe , Thr48Ile , Val75Met and Arg477Lys , were found in patients with <mark>congenital thrombocytopenia</mark> and no clinically evident immune defect indicating that the WASP gene is the site for mutations in <mark>X - linked thrombocytopenia</mark> as well as in <mark>WAS</mark> . 
A T - cell line from a <mark>WAS</mark> patient contained two independent DNA alterations , a constitutional frameshift mutation , also present in peripheral blood leukocytes from the patient , and compensatory splice site mutation unique to the cell line . 
The distribution of eight missense mutations provides valuable information on amino acids which are essential for normal protein function , and suggests that sites in the first two exons are hot - spots for mutation . 
Evidence for inter - generational instability in the CAG repeat in the MJD1 gene and for conserved haplotypes at flanking markers amongst Japanese and Caucasian subjects with <mark>Machado - Joseph disease</mark> . 
The size of the ( CAG ) n repeat array in the 3 ' end of the MJD1 gene and the haplotype at a series of microsatellite markers surrounding the MJD1 gene were examined in a large cohort of Japanese and Caucasian subjects affected with <mark>Machado - Joseph disease</mark> ( <mark>MJD</mark> ) . 
Our data provide five novel observations . 
First , <mark>MJD</mark> is associated with expansion fo the array from the normal range of 14 - 37 repeats to 68 - 84 repeats in most Japanese and Caucasian subjects , but no subjects were observed with expansions intermediate in size between those of the normal and <mark>MJD</mark> affected groups . 
Second , the expanded allele associated with <mark>MJD</mark> displays inter - generational instability , particularly in male meioses , and this instability was associated with the clinical phenomenon of anticipation . 
Third , the size of the expanded allele is not only inversely correlated with the age - of - onset of <mark>MJD</mark> ( r = - 0 . 738 , p < 0 . 001 ) , but is also correlated with the frequency of other clinical features [ e . g . pseudoexophthalmos and pyramidal signs were more frequent in subjects with large repeats ( p < 0 . 001 and p < 0 . 05 respectively ) ] . 
Fourth , the disease phenotype is significantly more severe and had an early age of onset ( 16 years ) in a subject homozygous for the expanded allele , which contrasts with <mark>Huntington disease</mark> and suggests that the expanded allele in the MJD1 gene could exert its effect either by a dominant negative effect ( putatively excluded in <mark>HD</mark> ) or by a gain of function effect as proposed for <mark>HD</mark> . 
Finally , Japanese and Caucasian subjects affected with <mark>MJD</mark> share haplotypes at several markers surrounding the MJD1 gene , which are uncommon in the normal Japanese and Caucasian population , and which suggests the existence either of common founders in these populations or of chromosomes susceptible to pathologic expansion of the CAG repeat in the MJD1 gene . 
A 4 - megabase YAC contig that spans the <mark>Langer - Giedion syndrome</mark> region on human chromosome 8q24 . 1 : use in refining the location of the <mark>trichorhinophalangeal syndrome</mark> and multiple exostoses genes ( TRPS1 and EXT1 ) . 
We have constructed a physical map covering over 4 Mb of human chromosome 8q24 . 
1 and used this map to refine the locations of the genes responsible for <mark>Langer - Giedion syndrome</mark> . 
The map is composed of overlapping YAC clones that were identified and ordered in relation to sequence tagged sites mapped to the Langer - Giedion chromosomal region on somatic cell hybrids . 
The minimal region of overlap of <mark>Langer - Giedion syndrome</mark> deletions , previously identified by analysis of 15 patients , was placed on the map by analysis of 2 patients whose deletions define the endpoints . 
The chromosome 8 breakpoint of a balanced t ( 8 ; 9 ) ( q24 . 11 ; q33 . 3 ) translocation from a patient with <mark>trichorhinophalangeal syndrome</mark> ( <mark>TRPS</mark> I ) was found to be located just within the proximal end of the minimal deletion region . 
A deletion of 8q24 . 
11 - q24 . 
3 in a patient with multiple exostoses was found to overlap the distal end of the <mark>LGS</mark> deletion region , indicating that the EXT1 gene is distal to the TRPS1 gene and supporting the hypothesis that <mark>Langer - Giedion syndrome</mark> is due to loss of functional copies of both the TRPS1 and the EXT1 genes 
BRCA1 mutations in a population - based sample of young women with <mark>breast cancer</mark> . 
BACKGROUND . 
Inherited mutations in the BRCA1 gene are associated with a high risk of <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> in some families . 
However , little is known about the contribution of BRCA1 mutations to <mark>breast cancer</mark> in the general population . 
We analyzed DNA samples from women enrolled in a population - based study of early - onset <mark>breast cancer</mark> to assess the spectrum and frequency of germ - line BRCA1 mutations in young women with <mark>breast cancer</mark> . 
METHODS . 
We studied 80 women in whom <mark>breast cancer</mark> was diagnosed before the age of 35 , and who were not selected on the basis of family history . 
Genomic DNA was studied for BRCA1 mutations by analysis involving single - strand conformation polymorphisms and with allele - specific assays . 
Alterations were defined by DNA sequencing . 
RESULTS . 
Germ - line BRCA1 mutations were identified in 6 of the 80 women . 
Four additional rare sequence variants of unknown functional importance were also identified . 
Two of the mutations and three of the rare sequence variants were found among the 39 women who reported no family history of <mark>breast or ovarian cancer</mark> . 
None of the mutations and only one of the rare variants was identified in a reference population of 73 unrelated subjects . 
CONCLUSIONS . 
Alterations in BRCA1 were identified in approximately 10 percent of this cohort of young women with <mark>breast cancer</mark> . 
The risk of harboring a mutation was not limited to women with family histories of <mark>breast or ovarian cancer</mark> . 
These results represent a minimal estimate of the frequency of BRCA1 mutations in this population . 
Comprehensive methods of identifying BRCA1 mutations and understanding their importance will be needed before testing of women in the general population can be undertaken . . 
Novel inherited mutations and variable expressivity of BRCA1 alleles , including the founder mutation 185delAG in Ashkenazi Jewish families . 
Thirty - seven families with four or more cases of <mark>breast cancer</mark> or <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> were analyzed for mutations in BRCA1 . 
Twelve different germ - line mutations , four novel and eight previously observed , were detected in 16 families . 
Five families of Ashkenazi Jewish descent carried the 185delAG mutation and shared the same haplotype at eight polymorphic markers spanning approximately 850 kb at BRCA1 . 
Expressivity of 185delAG in these families varied , from early - onset <mark>breast cancer</mark> without <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> . 
Mutation 4184delTCAA occurred independently in two families . 
In one family , penetrance was complete , with females developing early - onset <mark>breast cancer</mark> or <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> and the male carrier developing <mark>prostatic cancer</mark> , whereas , in the other family , penetrance was incomplete and only <mark>breast cancer</mark> occurred , diagnosed at ages 38 - 81 years . 
Two novel nonsense mutations led to the loss of mutant BRCA1 transcript in families with 10 and 6 cases of early - onset <mark>breast cancer</mark> and <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> . 
A 665 - nt segment of the BRCA1 3 - UTR and 1 . 
3 kb of genomic sequence including the putative promoter region were invariant by single - strand conformation analysis in 13 families without coding - sequence mutations . 
Overall in our series , BRCA1 mutations have been detected in 26 families 16 with positive BRCA1 lod scores , 7 with negative lod scores ( reflecting multiple sporadic <mark>breast cancers</mark> ) , and 3 not tested for linkage . 
Three other families have positive lod scores for linkage to BRCA2 , but 13 families without detected BRCA1 mutations have negative lod scores for both BRCA1 and BRCA2 . 
A new glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase variant , G6PD Orissa ( 44 Ala - - > Gly ) , is the major polymorphic variant in tribal populations in India . 
<mark>Deficiency of glucose - 6 - phosphate dehydrogenase</mark> ( G6PD ) is usually found at high frequencies in areas of the world where <mark>malaria</mark> has been endemic . 
The frequency and genetic basis of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> have been studied in Africa , around the Mediterranean , and in the Far East , but little such information is available about the situation in India . 
To determine the extent of heterogeneity of G6PD , we have studied several different Indian populations by screening for <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> , followed by molecular analysis of deficient alleles . 
The frequency of <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> varies between 3 % and 15 % in different tribal and urban groups . 
Remarkably , a previously unreported deficient variant , G6PD Orissa ( 44 Ala - - > Gly ) , is responsible for most of the <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> in tribal Indian populations but is not found in urban populations , where most of the <mark>G6PD deficiency</mark> is due to the G6PD Mediterranean ( 188 Ser - - > Phe ) variant . 
The KmNADP of G6PD Orissa is fivefold higher than that of the normal enzyme . 
This may be due to the fact that the alanine residue that is replaced by glycine is part of a putative coenzyme - binding site . . 
Evidence for linkage of <mark>bipolar disorder</mark> to chromosome 18 with a parent - of - origin effect . 
A susceptibility gene on chromosome 18 and a parent - of - origin effect have been suggested for <mark>bipolar affective disorder</mark> ( <mark>BPAD</mark> ) . 
We have studied 28 nuclear families selected for apparent unilineal transmission of the <mark>BPAD</mark> phenotype , by using 31 polymorphic markers spanning chromosome 18 . 
Evidence for linkage was tested with affected - sib - pair and LOD score methods under two definitions of the affected phenotype . 
The affected - sibpair analyses indicated excess allele sharing for markers on 18p within the region reported previously . 
The greatest sharing was at D18S37 64 % in bipolar and recurrent unipolar ( RUP ) sib pairs ( P = . 0006 ) . 
In addition , excess sharing of the paternally , but not maternally , transmitted alleles was observed at three markers on 18q at D18S41 , 51 bipolar and RUP sib pairs were concordant for paternally transmitted alleles , and 21 pairs were discordant ( P = 0004 ) . 
The evidence for linkage to loci on both 18p and 18q was strongest in the 11 paternal pedigrees , i . 
e e . , those in which the father or one of the fathers sibs is affected . 
In these pedigrees , the greatest allele sharing ( 81 % ; P = . 00002 ) and the highest LOD score ( 3 . 51 ; phi = 0 . 0 ) were observed at D18S41 . 
Our results provide further support for linkage of <mark>BPAD</mark> to chromosome 18 and the first molecular evidence for a parent - of - origin effect operating in this disorder . 
The number of loci involved , and their precise location , require further study 
A prevalent mutation for <mark>galactosemia</mark> among black Americans . 
OBJECTIVE To define the mutation causing <mark>galactosemia</mark> in patients of black American origin who have no galactose - 1 - phosphate uridyltransferase ( GALT ) activity in erythrocytes but good clinical outcome . 
METHODS We discovered a mutation caused by a C - - > T transition at base - pair 1158 of the GALT gene that results in a serine - to - leucine substitution at codon 135 ( S135L ) . 
We developed a method with which to screen populations for its prevalence . 
We compared galactose - 1 - phosphate uridyltransferase among erythrocytes , leukocytes , and transformed lymphoblasts , as well as total body oxidation of D - ( 13C ) - galactose to 13CO2 among three genotypes for GALT ( S135L / S135L , Q188R / Q188R , and Normal / Normal ) . 
RESULTS We found a 48 % prevalence of the S135L mutation among 17 black American patients with <mark>classic galactosemia</mark> and a 1 % prevalence in a population of 50 black Americans without <mark>galactosemia</mark> . 
The S135L mutation was not found in 84 white patients with G / G <mark>galactosemia</mark> nor in 87 white control subjects without <mark>galactosemia</mark> . 
We found normal whole body oxidation of D - ( 13C ) - galactose by the patient homozygous for S135L and various degrees of enzyme impairment among different tissues . 
CONCLUSIONS The S135L mutation in the GALT gene is a prevalent cause of <mark>galactosemia</mark> among black patients . 
Because GALT activity varies in different tissues of patients homozygous for S135L , they may have a better clinical outcome than patients who are homozygous for Q188R when both are treated from infancy . . 
A high incidence of BRCA1 mutations in 20 <mark>breast - ovarian cancer</mark> families . 
We have analyzed 20 <mark>breast - ovarian cancer</mark> families , the majority of which show positive evidence of linkage to chromosome 17q12 for germ - line mutations in the BRCA1 gene . 
BRCA1 mutations cosegregating with <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> susceptibility were identified in 16 families , including 1 family with a case of <mark>male breast cancer</mark> . 
Nine of these mutations have not been reported previously . 
The majority of mutations were found to generate a premature stop codon leading to the formation of a truncated BRCA1 protein of 2 % - 88 % of the expected normal length . 
Two mutations altered the RING finger domain . 
Sequencing of genomic DNA led to the identification of a mutation in the coding region of BRCA1 in 12 families , and cDNA analysis revealed an abnormal or missing BRCA1 transcript in 4 of the 8 remaining families . 
A total of eight mutations were associated with a reduced quantity of BRCA1 transcript . 
We were unable to detect BRCA1 mutations in 4 of the 20 families , but only 1 of these was clearly linked to BRCA1 . 
It is expected that the majority of clear examples of the <mark>breast - ovarian syndrome</mark> will be associated with germ - line mutations in the coding region of BRCA1 . . 
<mark>Brca1 deficiency</mark> results in early <mark>embryonic lethality</mark> characterized by <mark>neuroepithelial abnormalities</mark> . 
The <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> susceptibility gene , BRCA1 , has been cloned and shown to encode a zinc - finger protein of unknown function . 
Mutations in BRCA1 account for at least 80 % of families with both <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> , as well as some non - familial sporadic <mark>ovarian cancers</mark> . 
The loss of wild - type BRCA1 in <mark>tumours</mark> of individuals carrying one nonfunctional BRCA1 allele suggests that BRCA1 encodes a <mark>tumour</mark> suppressor that may inhibit the proliferation of mammary epithelial cells . 
To examine the role of BRCA1 in normal tissue growth and differentiation , and to generate a potential model for the <mark>cancer</mark> susceptibility associated with loss of BRCA1 function , we have created a mouse line carrying a mutation in one Brca1 allele . 
Analysis of mice homozygous for the mutant allele indicate that Brca1 is critical for normal development , as these mice died in utero between 10 and 13 days of gestation ( E10 - E13 ) . 
Abnormalities in <mark>Brca1 - deficient</mark> embryos were most evident in the neural tube , with 40 % of the embryos presenting with varying degrees of <mark>spina bifida</mark> and <mark>anencephaly</mark> . 
In addition , the neuroepithelium in <mark>Brca1 - deficient</mark> embryos appeared disorganized , with signs of both rapid proliferation and excessive cell death . . 
Identification of mutations in the ALD - gene of 20 families with <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> / <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> . 
<mark>Adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> ) , an <mark>X - linked inherited metabolic disorder</mark> , is the most frequent <mark>inborn peroxisomal disease</mark> . 
It leads to <mark>demyelination in the central and peripheral nervous system</mark> . 
Defective beta - oxidation of saturated very long chain fatty acids ( VLCFAs ; C22 0 - C26 0 ) in peroxisomes has been shown to lead to an accumulation of VLCFAs in leukoid areas of the central nervous system , peripheral nerves , adrenal gland , and blood . 
The <mark>ALD</mark> gene has been recently identified and encodes a 745 - amino - acid protein . 
We screened patients with <mark>adrenoleukodystrophy</mark> / <mark>adrenomyeloneuropathy</mark> ( <mark>ALD</mark> / <mark>AMN</mark> ) from 20 kindreds for mutations in the <mark>ALD</mark> gene . 
Eleven missense and two nonsense mutations , five deletions , and one insertion were detected by direct sequencing of eight reverse transcribed fragments of the <mark>ALD</mark> - gene mRNA . 
Four mutations could be shown to be de novo . 
All mutations could be confirmed in carriers by sequencing genomic DNA . 
No correlation between the type of mutation and the severity of the phenotype could be observed . 
The mutations were not detected in the <mark>ALD</mark> gene of 30 healthy persons . . 
The murine homolog of the human <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> susceptibility gene Brca1 maps to mouse chromosome 11D . 
The recently cloned human <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> susceptibility gene , BRCA1 , is located on human chromosome 17q21 . 
We have isolated murine genomic clones containing Brca1 as a first step in generating a mouse model for the loss of BRCA1 function . 
A mouse genomic library was screened using probes corresponding to exon 11 of the human BRCA1 gene . 
Two overlapping mouse clones were identified that hybridized to human BRCA1 exons 9 - 12 . 
Sequence analysis of 1 . 
4 kb of the region of these clones corresponding to part of human exon 11 revealed 72 % nucleic acid identity but only 50 % amino acid identity with the human gene . 
The longest of the mouse Brca1 genomic clones maps to chromosome 11D , as determined by two - color fluorescence in situ hybridization . 
The synteny to human chromosome 17 was confirmed by cohybridization with the mouse probe for the NF1 - gene . 
This comparative study confirms that the relative location of the BRCA1 gene has been conserved between mice and humans . 
<mark>Atelosteogenesis type II</mark> is caused by mutations in the <mark>diastrophic dysplasia</mark> sulfate - transporter gene ( DTDST ) : evidence for a phenotypic series involving three <mark>chondrodysplasias</mark> . 
<mark>Atelosteogenesis type II</mark> ( <mark>AO II</mark> ) is a neonatally lethal <mark>chondrodysplasia</mark> whose clinical and histological characteristics resemble those of another <mark>chondrodysplasia</mark> , the much less severe <mark>diastrophic dysplasia</mark> ( <mark>DTD</mark> ) . 
The similarity suggests a shared pathogenesis involving lesions in the same biochemical pathway and perhaps the same gene . 
<mark>DTD</mark> is caused by mutations in the recently identified <mark>diastrophic dysplasia</mark> sulfate - transporter gene ( DTDST ) . 
Here , we report that <mark>AOII</mark> patients also have DTDST mutations , which lead to defective uptake of inorganic sulfate and insufficient sulfation of macromolecules by patient mesenchymal cells in vitro . 
Together with our recent observation that a third even more severe <mark>chondrodysplasia</mark> , achondrogenesis type IB , is also caused by mutations in DTDST , these results demonstrate a phenotypic series of three <mark>chondrodysplasias</mark> of increasing severity caused by lesions in a single sulfate - transporter gene . 
The severity of the phenotype appears to be correlated with the predicted effect of the mutations on the residual activity of the DTDST protein . . 
Haplotype and phenotype analysis of six recurrent BRCA1 mutations in 61 families : results of an international study . 
Several BRCA1 mutations have now been found to occur in geographically diverse <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> families . 
To investigate mutation origin and mutation - specific phenotypes due to BRCA1 , we constructed a haplotype of nine polymorphic markers within or immediately flanking the BRCA1 locus in a set of 61 <mark>breast / ovarian cancer</mark> families selected for having one of six recurrent BRCA1 mutations . 
Tests of both mutations and family - specific differences in age at diagnosis were not significant . 
A comparison of the six mutations in the relative proportions of cases of <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> was suggestive of an effect ( P = . 069 ) , with 57 % of women presumed affected because of the 1294 del 40 BRCA1 mutation having <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> , compared with 14 % of affected women with the splice - site mutation in intron 5 of BRCA1 . 
For the BRCA1 mutations studied here , the individual mutations are estimated to have arisen 9 - 170 generations ago . 
In general , a high degree of haplotype conservation across the region was observed , with haplotype differences most often due to mutations in the short - tandem - repeat markers , although some likely instances of recombination also were observed . 
For several of the instances , there was evidence for multiple , independent , BRCA1 mutational events . 
Isolation of the mouse homologue of BRCA1 and genetic mapping to mouse chromosome 11 . 
The BRCA1 gene is in large part responsible for <mark>hereditary human breast and ovarian cancer</mark> . 
Here we report the isolation of the murine Brca1 homologue cDNA clones . 
In addition , we identified genomic P1 clones that contain most , if not all , of the mouse Brca1 locus . 
DNA sequence analysis revealed that the mouse and human coding regions are 75 % identical at the nucleotide level while the predicted amino acid identity is only 58 % . 
A DNA sequence variant in the Brca1 locus was identified and used to map this gene on a ( Mus m . musculus Czech II x C57BL / KsJ ) F1 x C57BL / KsJ intersubspecific backcross to distal mouse chromosome 11 . 
The mapping of this gene to a region highly syntenic with human chromosome 17 , coupled with Southern and Northern analyses , confirms that we isolated the murine Brca1 homologue rather than a related RING finger gene . 
The isolation of the mouse Brca1 homologue will facilitate the creation of mouse models for germline <mark>BRCA1 defects</mark> . . 
<mark>Emerin deficiency</mark> at the nuclear membrane in patients with <mark>Emery - Dreifuss muscular dystrophy</mark> . 
Mutations in the STA gene at the Xq28 locus have been found in patients with <mark>X - linked Emery - Dreifuss muscular dystrophy</mark> ( <mark>EDMD</mark> ) . 
This gene encodes a hitherto unknown protein named emerin . 
To elucidate the subcellular localization of emerin , we raised two antisera against synthetic peptide fragments predicted from emerin cDNA . 
Using both antisera , we found positive nuclear membrane staining in skeletal , cardiac and smooth muscles in the normal controls and in patients with <mark>neuromuscular diseases</mark> other than <mark>EDMD</mark> . 
In contrast , a deficiency in immunofluorescent staining of skeletal and cardiac muscle from <mark>EDMD</mark> patients was observed . 
A 34 kD protein is immunoreactive with the antisera - - the protein is equivalent to that predicted for emerin . 
Together , our findings suggest the specific <mark>deficiency of emerin</mark> in the nuclear membrane of muscle cells in patients with <mark>EDMD</mark> . . 
<mark>Growth retardation</mark> and <mark>tumour</mark> inhibition by BRCA1 . 
Inherited mutations in BRCA1 predispose to <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> , but the role of BRCA1 in sporadic <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> has previously been elusive . 
Here , we show that retroviral transfer of the wild - type BRCA1 gene inhibits growth in vitro of all <mark>breast and ovarian cancer</mark> cell lines tested , but not <mark>colon or lung cancer</mark> cells or fibroblasts . 
Mutant BRCA1 has no effect on growth of <mark>breast cancer</mark> cells ; <mark>ovarian cancer</mark> cell growth is not affected by BRCA1 mutations in the 5 portion of the gene , but is inhibited by 3 BRCA1 mutations . 
Development of <mark>MCF - 7 tumours</mark> in nude mice is inhibited when MCF - 7 cells are transfected with wild - type , but not mutant , BRCA1 . 
Most importantly , among mice with established <mark>MCF - 7 tumours</mark> , peritoneal treatment with a retroviral vector expressing wild - type BRCA1 significantly inhibits <mark>tumour</mark> growth and increased survival . .
